How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face subtle pressure to hide or downplay your beliefs in daily situations, which response from this story do you most resemble— fleeing, disavowing, or staying silent with certainty? Are you willing to endure isolation rather than compromise even a small truth? What is the strength of your yaqīn that would keep you from disavowing?
?
Think of a time you felt alone in holding a truth. Did you remain patient like al-Khabbazi or did you quietly let it go? This passage says he was 'clinging to the strength of his certainty'—what are you currently clinging to that gives you similar resolve? Is it rooted in genuine conviction or mere habit?
?
Al-Khabbazi stayed in his house, not fleeing or fighting. When the cost of integrity is high, do you have the courage to simply remain where you are without capitulating? What would it take for you to die patient upon your deen, with certainty as your only support? Are you building that certainty now?

Biography of Abu al-Fadl ibn Amrus al-Maliki
Ibn Asakir presents two testimonies on the life of the Maliki jurist Abu al-Fadl ibn Amrus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life and scholarly stature of Abu al-Fadl ibn Amrus, a leading Maliki jurist in Baghdad, as documented by Ibn Asakir through two chains of transmission.

Core Idea
Two testimonies confirm Abu al-Fadl ibn Amrus as the ultimate Maliki authority in Baghdad.

This passage from Ibn Asakir's Tabin Kidhb al-Muftari provides a biographical sketch of the Maliki jurist Abu al-Fadl ibn Amrus. Ibn Asakir cites two reliable sources: al-Khatib al-Baghdadi and Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi, both of whom attest to his deep knowledge, religious integrity, and central role in issuing fatwas in Baghdad. Through these testimonies, we gain insight into the scholarly recognition of a key figure in the Maliki school.

Guided Path
1
Understand the biographical context
Recognize that this passage is a composite biography using two chains of transmission (isnad). Ibn Asakir is carefully documenting the life of a Maliki scholar to preserve his legacy.
The first testimony comes from al-Khatib al-Baghdadi via three narrators; the second from Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi via one narrator.
2
Extract details from the first testimony
Al-Khatib describes Abu al-Fadl as a jurist, Qur'an memorizer, teacher, and the ultimate mufti for Maliki fiqh in Baghdad. Note his birth in 372 AH and death in 452 AH.
He was also accepted as a witness by the Chief Judge, highlighting his trustworthiness.
3
Extract details from the second testimony
Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi adds that he was a 'usuli' (scholar of usul al-fiqh) and righteous, confirming the same death year.
This brief testimony reinforces his reputation without adding contradictions.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why Ibn Asakir includes these testimonies in a book defending against accusations of fabrications. The reliable chains and consistent praise show the authenticity of Abu al-Fadl's scholarship.
This biography also serves as a historical source for Maliki presence in Baghdad.

And among them is Abu al-Fadl ibn Amrus al-Baghdadi al-Maliki, may God have mercy on him.
Al-Sharif Abu al-Qasim Ali ibn Ibrahim ibn al-Abbas al-Alawi, al-Shaykh Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Ahmad ibn Mansur al-Ghassani, and Abu Mansur ibn Khayrun informed us, saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Thabit al-Khatib al-Hafiz said: Muhammad ibn Ubayd Allah Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Amrus, Abu al-Fadl al-Bazzaz, was one of the jurists of the Maliki school, and he was also among the memorizers of the Quran and its teachers. He heard from Abu al-Qasim ibn Hababa, Abu Hafs ibn Shahin, Abu Tahir al-Mukhlis, and Abu al-Qasim ibn al-Saydalani. I wrote from him, and he was religious, trustworthy, and discreet. The fatwa in jurisprudence according to Malik in Baghdad ended with him. The Chief Judge Abu Abd Allah al-Damghani accepted his testimony. He resided at Bab al-Sham. I asked Abu al-Fadl about his birth, and he said in Rajab of the year 372. And we learned while in Damascus that he died at the beginning of Muharram of the year 452.
From

Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage is a composite biography of Abu al-Fadl ibn Amrus, a prominent Maliki scholar in Baghdad. It contains two testimonies: first, from al-Khatib al-Baghdadi, who praises him as a jurist, Qur'an memorizer, teacher, and the ultimate authority for Maliki fatwa in Baghdad. He also notes his birth in 372 AH and death in 452 AH. Second, from Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi, who simply confirms his status as a jurist, usuli (scholar of usul al-fiqh), and righteous person, with the same death year. The biography emphasizes his reliability and the high regard of contemporary judges.

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir

Biography of al-Ustadh Abu al-Qasim al-Isfarayini
Ibn Asakir records the biography of al-Isfarayini, highlighting his scholarship and piety.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life and scholarly stature of al-Isfarayini, a key Ash'ari theologian and teacher of Imam al-Haramayn.

Core Idea
Al-Isfarayini was a peerless Ash'ari scholar who combined deep theology with ascetic piety.

This lesson introduces you to one of the great Ash'ari figures, Abu al-Qasim al-Isfarayini. Through a biographical notice by Ibn Asakir, we learn about his epithets, his role as an imam of the duwayra of Bayhaq, and his influence on later scholars, especially Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni. The passage highlights his excellence in kalam and his adherence to the way of the salaf.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get a sense of the subject's life and character.
2
Identify the key attributes and titles
Note the epithets: al-Asamm (the deaf), al-Iskaff (the shoemaker), and his affiliation with Ash'aris.
These titles often indicate a distinguishing trait or profession.
3
Connect his teaching to Imam al-Haramayn
Understand that al-Isfarayini was the teacher of Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni, a major figure in Ash'ari theology.
This shows his influence on later generations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم الأستاذ أبو القسم الاسفراینی رحمه الله )
كتب إلى الشيخ أبو الحسن عبد الغافر بن إسماعيل بن عبد الغافر الفارسي قال : عبد الجبارين على بن محمد بن حسكان الأستاذ الإمام أبو القسم المتكلم الاسفراينى الأصم ؛ المعروف بالاسكاف ، شيخ كبير جليل من أفاضل العصر ورؤس الفقهاء والمتكلمين من أصحاب الأشعرى ، إمام دويرة البيهقى له اللسان في النظر والتدريس والقدم فى الفتوى مع لزوم طريقة السلف من الزهد والفقر والورع كان عديم النظير في فنه ما رؤى مثله ، قرأ عليه إمام الحرمين الأصول وتخرج بطريقته عاش عالما عاملا ، وتوفى يوم الاثنين الثامن والعشرين من صفر سنة اثنتين وخمسين وأربعمائة
And among them is al-Ustadh Abu al-Qasim al-Isfarayini, may God have mercy on him.
Al-Shaykh Abu al-Hasan Abd al-Ghafir ibn Isma'il ibn Abd al-Ghafir al-Farisi wrote to me, saying: Abd al-Jabbarayn Ali ibn Muhammad ibn Hiskan [al-Ustadh al-Imam Abu al-Qasim] al-Mutakallim al-Isfarayini al-Asamm, known as al-Iskaff, a great and noble shaykh, one of the most excellent of the age and the leaders of the jurists and theologians among the followers of al-Ash'ari, imam of the duwayra of Bayhaq, had eloquence in theoretical investigation and teaching, and precedence in fatwa, while adhering to the way of the salaf in asceticism, poverty, and piety. He was without peer in his field; no one like him was seen. Imam al-Haramayn read usul under him and graduated in his method. He lived as a scholar and practitioner, and died on Monday, the 28th of Safar, year 452.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage is a biographical notice on al-Ustadh Abu al-Qasim al-Isfarayini (also known as al-Asamm or al-Iskaff), a prominent Ash'ari theologian and Shafi'i jurist. It describes him as a leading figure among the Ash'aris, an imam of the duwayra (school or monastery) of Bayhaq, skilled in kalam and teaching. He adhered to the way of the salaf in zuhd, faqr, and wara'. Notably, Imam al-Haramayn (al-Juwayni) studied usul al-din under him and followed his method. His death date is given as 28 Safar 452 AH. The text emphasizes his unparalleled excellence and his combination of scholarship and action.

Key Terms
الأستاذ أبو القاسم الإسفراييني
الأصم
الإسكاف
أصحاب الأشعري
دويرة البيهقي
إمام الحرمين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The title 'الأصم' (the deaf) might be misinterpreted as a literal disability, but it is likely a nickname. Also, 'دويرة البيهقى' is a specific institution, not a generic term.
Correction: Al-Asamm is a common epithet in biographical literature, not necessarily indicating a physical condition. Duwayra al-Bayhaqi is a known location or institution in Bayhaq, not a generic phrase.

Checkpoint
Who studied usul under al-Isfarayini according to this biography?
A) Abu Bakr al-Bayhaqi
B) Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni
C) Al-Khatib al-Baghdadi
D) Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi

Key Takeaway
Al-Isfarayini was a leading Ash'ari scholar who taught Imam al-Haramayn and was known for his combination of kalam expertise and ascetic piety.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Isfarayini was praised as both a scholar and a practitioner ('aaliman 'aamilan). In what area of your life have you been content to know without acting? What specific action will you take this week to live out what you know?
?
You read that he was 'without peer in his field' and that no one like him was seen. What field of Islamic knowledge has Allah entrusted you with? Are you striving for excellence in it, or have you become complacent? What one change will you make today to raise your standard?
?
Imam al-Haramayn graduated under al-Isfarayini's method. Who are you learning from, and are you truly absorbing their method or just skimming information? How can you become a more disciplined student this month?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner

The Life and Praise of Imam al-Bayhaqi
Biography with birth, death, and Juwayni's praise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key biographical details of Imam al-Bayhaqi and the unique praise he received from Imam al-Juwayni.

Core Idea
Al-Bayhaqi is so distinguished that al-Juwayni says he has a favor upon al-Shafi'i himself.

Imam Ibn Asakir begins the biography of al-Bayhaqi with the basic facts of his birth and death, but immediately follows with a striking testimony from Imam al-Juwayni. This sets al-Bayhaqi apart from every other Shafi'i scholar—his works actually benefit the founder of the school. Let's read this passage to see how al-Bayhaqi's legacy is introduced.

Guided Path
1
Read the birth and death dates
Note when al-Bayhaqi was born (384 AH) and when he died (458 AH). These dates place him in the 4th-5th centuries, a golden age of hadith scholarship.
His lifespan of 74 years saw extensive travel and learning.
2
Understand al-Juwayni's statement
Al-Juwayni, a leading Shafi'i scholar, says that every Shafi'i owes a favor to al-Shafi'i except al-Bayhaqi, who instead has a favor upon al-Shafi'i. This means al-Bayhaqi's writings strengthened the madhhab.
This is an extraordinary compliment, highlighting al-Bayhaqi's unique contribution.
3
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself: Why would al-Juwayni say this? How did al-Bayhaqi's works serve the Shafi'i school in a way no other scholar did?
Think about his book al-Ma'rifa and other works that defended Shafi'i positions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم أبو بكر النيسابورى البيهقى الحافظ رحمه الله
قال لنا الشيخ أبو بكر البغدادى قال لنا أبو على إسماعيل بن أحمد مولد والدى الإمام شيخ السنة أبى بكر البيهقي في شعبان سنة أربع وثمانين وثلاثماية وتوفي في جمادى الأولى سنة ثمان وخمسين وأربعمائة . سمعت الشيخ أبا بكر محمد بن عبد الله بن أحمد بن أحمد بن حبيب العامرى ببغداد يقول سمعت من يحكى عن الإمام أبي المعالي الجويني أنه قال : ما من شافعى إلا وللشافعي عليه منة إلا أحمد البيهقي فإن له على الشافعي منة لتصانيفه في نصرة مذهبه وأقاويله أو كما قال . كتب إلى الشيخ أبو الحسن الفارسي قال : أحمد بن الحسين بن على ابن عبد الله بن موسى أبو بكر البيهقي الإمام الحافظ الفقيه الأصولي الدين الورع واحد زمانه في الحفظ ، وفرد أقرانه فى الاتقان والضبط ، من كبار أصحاب الحاكم أبي عبد الله الحافظ والمكثرين عنه ثم الزائد عليه في أنواع العلوم ، كتب الحديث وحفظه من صباه إلى أن نشأ وتفقه وبرع فيه وشرع في الأصول ورحل إلي العراق والجبال والحجاز ثم اشتغل بالتصنيف ، والف من الكتب ما لعله يبلغ قريباً من ألف جزء مما لم يسبقه إليه أحد ، جمع في تصانيفه بين علم الحديث والفقه وبيان علل الحديث والـصـحـيـح والسقيم ، وذكر وجوه الجمع بين الأحاديث ثم بيان الفقه والأصول وشرح ما يتعلق بالعربية ، استدعى منه الأئمة في عصره الانتقال إلى نيسابور من الناحية لسماع كتاب المعرفة وغير ذلك من تصانيفه فعاد إلى نيسابور سنة إحدى وأربعين وأربعمائة ، وعقدوا له المجلس لقراءة كتاب المعرفة وحضره
And among them is Abu Bakr al-Naysaburi al-Bayhaqi al-Hafiz, may God have mercy on him.
Al-Shaykh Abu Bakr al-Baghdadi said to us: Abu Ali Isma'il ibn Ahmad told us: The birth of my father, the Imam, the Shaykh of the Sunnah, Abu Bakr al-Bayhaqi, was in Sha'ban of the year 384, and he died in Jumada al-Ula of the year 458. I heard al-Shaykh Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Abd Allah ibn Ahmad ibn Ahmad ibn Habib al-Amiri in Baghdad saying: I heard someone relating from al-Imam Abu al-Ma'ali al-Juwayni that he said: There is no Shafi'i except that al-Shafi'i has a favor upon him, except Ahmad al-Bayhaqi, for he has a favor upon al-Shafi'i due to his writings in support of his school and his sayings, or as he said. Al-Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Farisi wrote to me, saying: Ahmad ibn al-Husayn ibn Ali ibn Abd Allah ibn Musa, Abu Bakr al-Bayhaqi, the imam, the hafiz, the faqih, the usuli, the religious, the pious, the unique of his time in memorization, the peerless among his contemporaries in precision and accuracy, one of the major companions of al-Hakim Abu Abd Allah al-Hafiz and the most prolific among them, then the one who surpassed him in various fields of knowledge. He wrote hadith and memorized it from his youth until he grew, studied fiqh, excelled in it, began [studying] usul, traveled to Iraq, the mountains, and the Hijaz, then occupied himself with authorship. He authored books, the number of which nearly reaches a thousand parts, something no one had preceded him in. In his writings, he combined the science of hadith and fiqh, the explanation of hadith defects, the sound and the weak, mentioned ways of reconciling hadith, then exposition of fiqh and usul, and explanation of what pertains to Arabic. The imams of his time requested him to move to Nishapur from the region to hear the book 'al-Ma'rifa' and other of his works, so he returned to Nishapur in the year 441. They organized a session for the reading of 'al-Ma'rifa', and he attended it.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive biography of Abu Bakr al-Bayhaqi, a towering figure in hadith and Shafi'i fiqh. It begins with his birth (384 AH) and death (458 AH) as reported by his son. A striking anecdote from Imam al-Juwayni states that al-Bayhaqi is the only Shafi'i upon whom al-Shafi'i has a favor reversed—i.e., al-Bayhaqi's writings actually benefitted al-Shafi'i's school. Then a detailed description from al-Farisi lauds his unmatched memory, precision, and prolific authorship (nearly 1000 volumes), his combining of hadith criticism with fiqh, his travel for knowledge, and his eventual move to Nishapur in 441 AH at the request of scholars to teach his book al-Ma'rifa. The biography highlights his mastery in hadith, usul, and Arabic, and his role as a defender of the Shafi'i school.

Key Terms
أبو بكر البيهقي
الحافظ
إمام الحرمين الجويني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Juwayni, how is Ahmad al-Bayhaqi unique among Shafi'is?
A) He was the first Shafi'i
B) He has a favor upon al-Shafi'i through his writings
C) He disagreed with al-Shafi'i on all matters
D) He was a student of al-Shafi'i

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Bayhaqi was born in 384 AH, died in 458 AH, and is the only Shafi'i scholar of whom Imam al-Juwayni said he has a favor upon al-Shafi'i due to his defensive writings.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Bayhaqi dedicated his writings to defending the school of al-Shafi'i, to the extent that al-Juwayni said he had a favor upon al-Shafi'i. What concrete action are you currently taking — or could you begin today — to defend and preserve the Islamic knowledge you have received, rather than just being a passive consumer of it?
?
Al-Bayhaqi's work 'al-Ma'rifa' and others are said to have supported al-Shafi'i's sayings. Whom in your life have you supported with your own skills or knowledge? If you cannot name a single person, what is holding you back from being a source of 'favor' to those who have taught you?
?
The praise from al-Juwayni is extraordinary because it reverses the usual gratitude. Think of a scholar, teacher, or parent who has shaped your faith. In what ways could you someday be the one who leaves a 'favor upon them' by spreading their teachings or correcting misunderstandings about them? Write down one specific step you will take this week.

The Scholarly Legacy of al-Bayhaqi
Detailed description of al-Bayhaqi's scholarship and authorship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the breadth of Imam al-Bayhaqi's scholarship—his mastery in hadith, fiqh, usul, and his prolific authorship of nearly 1000 volumes.

Core Idea
Al-Bayhaqi combined hadith criticism, fiqh, and usul in his writings, unmatched in quantity and quality.

After highlighting the Juwayni praise, Ibn Asakir provides a detailed description of al-Bayhaqi's scholarly profile from al-Farisi. It paints a picture of a scholar who was not only a hafiz of hadith but also a faqih, usuli, and prolific author whose works integrated multiple sciences. Let's read this passage to appreciate his legacy.

Guided Path
1
Identify his scholarly titles
Notice how al-Farisi describes him: imam, hafiz, faqih, usuli, religious, pious. These terms show his comprehensive mastery.
He was unique in his time in memorization (hifz) and precision (itqan).
2
Trace his educational journey
He began with hadith from youth, then studied fiqh, excelled, then usul, and traveled to Iraq, the mountains, and Hijaz to learn.
This shows his dedication to acquiring knowledge from multiple centers.
3
Appreciate his authorship
He wrote nearly 1000 parts, combining hadith, fiqh, hadith defects, reconciliation of hadith, and usul. His works integrated disciplines.
His book al-Ma'rifa was so important that scholars requested his move to Nishapur to hear it.
4
Reflect on his move to Nishapur
In 441 AH, he relocated to Nishapur at the request of the imams to teach al-Ma'rifa. This indicates his high status.

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner
5 min
Ibn Asakir's Praise of al-Khatib al-Baghdadi
Ibn Asakir extols al-Khatib al-Baghdadi's comprehensive mastery of hadith sciences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the high scholarly rank of al-Khatib al-Baghdadi as attested by Ibn Asakir, and the specific hadith categories he mastered.

Core Idea
Al-Khatib al-Baghdadi was the unmatched hadith authority in Baghdad after al-Daraqutni.

In this passage, the great Shafi'i hadith scholar Ibn Asakir offers a glowing testimonial of al-Khatib al-Baghdadi's erudition. He lists the precise areas of hadith science al-Khatib excelled in, from memorization to expertise in various hadith categories. This lesson will help you appreciate the stature of al-Khatib through the eyes of his contemporaries.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to get the overall testimonial.
Notice the extensive list of technical terms.
2
Identify the qualities praised
Ibn Asakir lists several qualities: knowledge (ma'rifa), mastery (itqān), memorization (hifẓ), precision (ḍabṭ), versatility (tafannun), and expertise (khibra). Understand each term's significance in hadith scholarship.
These are not random; they represent the highest levels of hadith mastery.
3
Understand the comparison to al-Daraqutni
Ibn Asakir states that after al-Daraqutni, no Baghdadi equaled al-Khatib. This places al-Khatib in the lineage of the greatest hadith scholars.
Al-Daraqutni (d. 385 AH) was a towering figure in hadith criticism.
4
Reflect on Ibn Asakir's personal benefit
Ibn Asakir acknowledges learning from al-Khatib's guidance. This shows the teacher-student transmission chain and the humility of scholars.
Even great scholars like Ibn Asakir recognize their debt to predecessors.
5
Note the concluding du'a
The passage ends with a prayer for reward for al-Khatib, all shaykhs, and all Muslims. This reflects the Islamic ethos of gratitude and supplication.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كان أبو بكر أحمد بن على بن ثابت الخطيب البغدادي، كان أحد الأعيان ممن شاهدناه معرفة وإتقاناً وحفظاً وضبطاً لحديث رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وتفنناً في عالمه وأسانيده، وخبرة برواته وناقليه، وعلماً بصحيحه وغريبه وفرده ومنكره وسقيمه ومطروحه، ولم يكن للبغداديين بعد أبي الحسن على بن عمر الدارقطني من يجرى مجراه ولا قام بعده منهم بهذا الشأن سواه، وقد أستفدنا كثيراً من هذا اليسير الذي نحسنه به وعنه، وتعلمنا شطراً من هذا القليل الذي نعرفه بتنبيهه ومنه، فجزاه الله تعالى عنا الخير ولقاه الحسنى والجميع مشايخنا وأئمتنا ولجميع المسلمين
Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn 'Ali ibn Thabit al-Khatib al-Baghdadi was one of the notable figures we witnessed in knowledge, mastery, memorization, and precision of the hadith of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), and versatility in his sciences and chains of transmission, and expertise in its transmitters and narrators, and knowledge of its sound, rare, solitary, rejected, defective, and discarded [hadiths]. There was none among the Baghdadis after Abu al-Hasan 'Ali ibn 'Umar al-Daraqutni who equaled him, nor did anyone after him arise among them in this field besides him. We have greatly benefited from this small amount that we have improved through him and from him, and we have learned a portion of this little that we know by his guidance and method. May Allah reward him well for us, and grant him goodness and beauty, and to all our shaykhs and imams, and to all Muslims.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage is a eulogy and testimonial. Ibn Asakir (or his source) describes al-Khatib al-Baghdadi's comprehensive mastery of hadith sciences, listing his expertise in categories like sound (sahih), rare (gharib), solitary (fard), rejected (munkar), defective (saqim), and discarded (matruh). He then declares that after al-Daraqutni, no Baghdadi equaled him. Finally, Ibn Asakir acknowledges personal benefit from al-Khatib's knowledge and prays for reward for him and all scholars.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think this praise implies al-Khatib was infallible or sinless.
Correction: The passage praises his scholarly rank, not prophetic or angelic status. Scholars can be outstanding yet still human and fallible.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Asakir, who was the last great hadith scholar in Baghdad before al-Khatib al-Baghdadi?
A) Ahmad ibn Hanbal
B) Abu al-Hasan al-Daraqutni
C) Abu al-Faraj ibn al-Armanazi
D) Abu al-Qasim Makki al-Maqdisi

Key Takeaway
Ibn Asakir's testimonial establishes al-Khatib al-Baghdadi as the foremost hadith scholar in Baghdad after al-Daraqutni, with mastery spanning all major hadith categories.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Ibn Asakir humbly acknowledged that he learned 'a portion' of his knowledge from al-Khatib. When was the last time you genuinely thanked a teacher for a specific thing they taught you? What prevented you from doing so? Make a concrete plan to express that gratitude this week.
?
The passage lists six categories of hadith that al-Khatib mastered. Do you have even basic familiarity with these terms? If not, what does that say about your own investment in learning the Prophet's sunnah? Commit today to studying one term deeply.
?
Imagine you had to write a testimonial for the person who taught you the most about your faith. Would your praise be as detailed and specific as Ibn Asakir's, or would it be vague? How can you learn to recognize and articulate the specific gifts your teachers have given you?

Dream Vision of Prophet Attending al-Khatib's Lecture
A dream vision of the Prophet attending al-Khatib's history lecture

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a dream vision defended the study of history and honored Imam al-Khatib.

Core Idea
A dream of the Prophet validated the study of history against its critics.

This lesson relates a remarkable dream in which the Prophet Muhammad attended a lecture on history given by Imam al-Khatib. The dreamer interpreted this as a divine endorsement of historical scholarship and a refutation of those who accused historians of bias. The passage also highlights al-Khatib's devotion to Quran recitation on Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Read the two anecdotes
Read the passage once to get the overall story. There are two parts: al-Khatib's practice on Hajj, and the dream vision of the Prophet attending his lecture.
Pay attention to the dreamer's reaction.
2
Understand al-Khatib's devotion
Note that al-Khatib would complete a full Quran recitation daily with tartil, then narrate hadith to people. This shows his scholarly dedication.
3
Analyze the dream vision
In the dream, the Prophet is present at a history lecture. The dreamer interprets this as an honor for al-Khatib and a refutation of those who criticize history for bias.
Think about why a dream could be seen as a proof for the value of history.
4
Reflect on the lesson's significance
Consider how this story defends the field of historical scholarship against its detractors. It shows that even the Prophet endorses the study of history when conducted by reliable scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أنبأنا الشيخ أبو الفرج بن أبي الحسن ابن الأرمنازى قال ثنا أبو الفرج الاسفرايني قال كان الشيخ أبو بكر الخطيب معنا في طريق الحج فكان يختم كل يوم ختمة إلى قرب الغياب قراءة بترتيل ثم يجتمع عليه الناس وهو راكب يقولون حدثنا فيحدثهم أو كما قال. وقال أبو الفرج أيضاً قال أبو القسم مكي بن عبد السلام المقدسي : كنت نائماً في منزل الشيخ أبي الحسن بن الزعفرانى ببغداد ليلة الأحد الثاني عشر من شهر ربيع الأول سنة ثلاث وستين وأربعمائة، فرأيت فى المنام عند السحر كأنا أجتمعنا عند الشيخ الإمام أبي بكر الخطيب فى منزله بباب المراتب لقراءة التاريخ على العادة، فكان الشيخ الإمام أبا بكر جالس والشيخ الفقيه أبو الفتح نصر بن إبراهيم عن يمينه وعن يمين الفقيه نصر رجل جالس لم أعرفه، فسألت عنه هذا الرجل الذى لم تجر عادته بالحضور معنا فقيل لي هذا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم جاء ليسمع التاريخ فقلت في نفسي هذه جلالة للشيخ أبى بكر إذ يحضر النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم مجلسه، وقلبت في نفسى وهذا أيضاً رد لقول من يعيب التاريخ ويذكر أن فيه تحاملاً على أقوام، وشغلنى التفكر فى هذا عن النهوض إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وسؤاله عن أشياء كنت قد قلت في نفسي أسأله عنها فانتبهت في الحال ولم أكلمه صلى الله عليه وسلم.
The shaykh Abu al-Faraj ibn Abi al-Hasan ibn al-Armanazi informed us, saying: Abu al-Faraj al-Isfarayini narrated to us, saying: The shaykh Abu Bakr al-Khatib was with us on the road to Hajj, and he would complete a full recitation (khatma) every day until near sunset, reading with tartil. Then people would gather around him while he was riding, saying: 'Narrate to us,' and he would narrate to them—or as he said. And Abu al-Faraj also said: Abu al-Qasim Makki ibn 'Abd al-Salam al-Maqdisi said: I was sleeping in the house of the shaykh Abu al-Hasan ibn al-Za'farani in Baghdad on the night of Sunday, the twelfth of Rabi' al-Awwal, in the year 463 AH. I saw in a dream near dawn as if we had gathered at the shaykh al-Imam Abu Bakr al-Khatib in his house at Bab al-Maratib to read the History (al-Tarikh) as usual. The shaykh al-Imam Abu Bakr was sitting, and the shaykh al-Faqih Abu al-Fath Nasr ibn Ibrahim was to his right, and to the right of al-Faqih Nasr was a man sitting whom I did not recognize. I asked about him: 'This man who is not accustomed to attending with us?' It was said to me: 'This is the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) who came to listen to the History.' I said to myself: 'This is an honor for the shaykh Abu Bakr, as the Prophet (peace be upon him) attends his gathering.' And I reflected to myself: 'This is also a refutation of the statement of those who criticize the History and claim that it contains bias against some people.' My preoccupation with this reflection distracted me from rising to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and asking him about things I had intended to ask him. So I woke up immediately without having spoken to him (peace be upon him).
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage contains two anecdotes. First, al-Khatib’s daily practice during Hajj: he would complete a full Quran recitation with slow, measured reading (tartil) by late afternoon, then narrate hadith to people while mounted. Second, a dream vision: Abu al-Qasim saw the Prophet Muhammad attending al-Khatib’s history reading. The dreamer interprets this as both an honor for al-Khatib and a refutation of those who criticize historical works for alleged bias (tahammul). The vision underscores the legitimacy and divine approval of the study of history when conducted by reliable scholars.

Key Terms
التاريخ
التحامل
الختمة
الترتيل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The dream proves the infallibility of the historian al-Khatib or that his work is beyond criticism.
Correction: The dream is a symbolic endorsement of the discipline of history itself, not a blanket approval of every individual or work. It refutes the general accusation of bias against historians, but does not make any particular historian infallible.

Checkpoint
Why did the dreamer consider the Prophet's attendance a refutation of criticism?
A) Because critics said history is forbidden
B) Because critics claimed history contains bias against people
C) Because critics denied the Prophet's knowledge
D) Because critics said al-Khatib was unreliable

Key Takeaway
The dream vision of the Prophet attending a lecture on history served as a powerful refutation of critics and affirmed the value of historical scholarship.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever dismissed a field of Islamic knowledge—like history, biography, or fiqh—as unimportant? What made you think that, and how does this dream challenge your assumption? This week, will you commit to learning one new thing about the history of our scholars?
?
The dreamer missed asking the Prophet (peace be upon him) because he was preoccupied with his own thoughts. In your daily life, are there moments when your intellectual reflections or distractions prevent you from directly engaging with the Quran and Sunnah? What specific step will you take to prioritize that connection?
?
The Prophet himself attended a lecture on history. How seriously do you take the study of Islamic history in your own learning? If it is not a priority, what is holding you back? Make one concrete plan to incorporate more historical study into your routine.

Death, Funeral, and Legacy of al-Khatib al-Baghdadi
Account of al-Khatib's death, burial, and scholarly legacy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the details of al-Khatib al-Baghdadi's death, his charitable acts, the public recognition of his defense of the Prophet, his burial, and his scholarly legacy.

Core Idea
Al-Khatib al-Baghdadi's funeral was a public testament to his lifelong defense of hadith and the Prophet.

This passage from Ibn 'Asakir's Tabyin Kidhb al-Muftari provides a firsthand obituary of the great hadith scholar al-Khatib al-Baghdadi. It records not only the date and circumstances of his death but also his final acts of charity, the outpouring of public grief, and the specific praises shouted by mourners. As you read, note how the account highlights his dedication to preserving the Prophet's authentic teachings and the lasting impact of his scholarly output.

Guided Path
1
Read the obituary notice
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the chain of transmission and the multiple details given about al-Khatib's death and funeral.
2
Identify acts of charity
The passage mentions three specific charitable acts: donating his money, clothing, and books. Reflect on how these reflect his priorities.
3
Note the public acclamation
The people praised him as a defender of the Prophet. Consider why this was so emphasized in the funeral procession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قرأت بخط الشيخ الأمين أبي الفضل أحمد بن الحسن بن خيرون الباقلاني ببغداد سنة ثلاث وستين وأربعمائة؛ مات أبو بكر أحمد بن علی بن ثابت ابن أحمد بن مهدى الخطيب الحافظ ضحوة نهار يوم الاثنين ودفن يوم ذى الحجة بباب حرب إلى جنب بشر بن الحرث؛ وصلى عليه من الثلاثاء في جامع المنصور وصلى عليه القاضي أبو الحسين محمد بن علی بن المهتدى بالله، وتصدق بجميع ماله وهو مايتا دينار وفرق ذلك على أصحاب الحديث والفقهاء والفقراء فى مرضه، ووصى أن يتصدق بجميع ما يخلفه من ثياب وغيرها وأوقف جميع كتبه على المسلمين وأخرجت جنازته من حجرة تلى المدرسة النظامية من نهر معلى وتبعه الفقهاء والخلق العظيم وحملت الجنازة وعبر بها على الجسر، وحملت إلى جامع المنصور وكان بين يدى الجنازة جماعة ينادون: هذا الذي كان يذب عن رسول الله صلی الله عليه وسلم، هذا الذي كان ينفى الكذب عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، هذا الذي كان يحفظ حديث رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وعبر بالجنازة فى الكرخ ومعها الخلق العظيم وكان اجتماع الناس في جامع المنصور وحضر جميع الفقهاء وأهل العلم ونقيب النقباء وتبع الجنازة خلق عظيم إلى باب حرب، وختم على القبر ختمات رضي الله عنه وغفر له وألحقه بعباده الصالحين، فلقد أنتهى إليه علم الحديث وحفظه، له ستة وخمسون مصنفاً في علم الحديث فمنها (تاريخ بغداد) مائة وستة أجزاء ولد سنة إحدى وتسعين وثلاثمائة. أخبرنا الشيخ الأمين أبو محمد هبة الله. ابن أحمد الأكفانى، قال ثنا أبو محمد عبد العزيز بن أحمد الكتاني الحافظ قال وردت كتب جماعة من بغداد إلى دمشق، كل واحد يذكر في كتابه أن الإمام الحافظ أبا بكر أحمد بن علی بن ثابت بن أحمد بن مهدی الخطيب البغدادي رحمه الله توفى يوم الاثنين ضحى نهار السابع من ذى الحجة من سنة ثلاث وستين وأربعمائة، وحمل يوم الثلاثاء إلى الجانب الغربي ودفن بالقرب من قبر أحمد بن حنبل عند قبر بشر بن الحرث
I read in the handwriting of the trustworthy shaykh Abu al-Fadl Ahmad ibn al-Hasan ibn Khayrun al-Baqillani in Baghdad in the year 463 AH: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn 'Ali ibn Thabit ibn Ahmad ibn Mahdi al-Khatib al-Hafiz died in the forenoon of Monday and was buried on Tuesday [during] Dhu al-Hijjah at Bab Harb beside Bishr ibn al-Harith. The funeral prayer was performed over him in the mosque of al-Mansur, and the judge Abu al-Husayn Muhammad ibn 'Ali ibn al-Muhtadi billah led the prayer. He gave in charity all his wealth, which was two hundred dinars, and distributed that to the hadith scholars, jurists, and poor during his illness. He willed that all his remaining clothes and other possessions be given in charity, and he endowed all his books to the Muslims. His funeral procession was brought out from a room adjacent to the Nizamiyya School from Nahr Mu'alla, and the jurists and a great multitude followed him. The funeral was carried and crossed the bridge, and was carried to the mosque of al-Mansur. In front of the funeral there were a group calling out: 'This is the one who defended the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him); this is the one who refuted falsehood about the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him); this is the one who preserved the hadith of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him).' The funeral passed through al-Karkh with a great multitude. The people gathered in the mosque of al-Mansur, and all the jurists, scholars, and the chief of the nobles attended. A great multitude followed the funeral to Bab Harb. Seals were placed on the grave repeatedly. May Allah be pleased with him, forgive him, and join him with His righteous servants. He had indeed attained the pinnacle of hadith knowledge and memorization. He authored fifty-six works on hadith, among them 'Tarikh Baghdad' in one hundred and six volumes. He was born in the year 391 AH. The trustworthy shaykh Abu Muhammad Hibatullah ibn Ahmad al-Akfani informed us, saying: Abu Muhammad 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn Ahmad al-Kattani al-Hafiz narrated to us, saying: Letters from a group in Baghdad arrived in Damascus, each one mentioning in his letter that the imam al-hafiz Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn 'Ali ibn Thabit ibn Ahmad ibn Mahdi al-Khatib al-Baghdadi, may Allah have mercy on him, died on Monday forenoon on the seventh of Dhu al-Hijjah in the year 463 AH, and was carried on Tuesday to the western side and buried near the grave of Ahmad ibn Hanbal by the grave of Bishr ibn al-Harith.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage is a detailed obituary and biographical notice. It records the date and circumstances of al-Khatib's death, his charitable acts (giving away all his money, clothes, and endowing his library), the large funeral procession with public acclamations of his defense of the Prophet, his burial near Ahmad ibn Hanbal and Bishr al-Harith, his scholarly output (56 works including Tarikh Baghdad in 106 volumes), and his birth year (391 AH). A second report confirms the death date. The account emphasizes his piety and his role as a defender of hadith.

Key Terms
الحافظ
الوقف
التصدق
تاريخ بغداد
المصنفات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many works did al-Khatib al-Baghdadi author in hadith according to this passage?
A) Fifty-six
B) Sixty-six
C) One hundred and six
D) Two hundred

Key Takeaway
Al-Khatib al-Baghdadi's death and funeral were marked by public recognition of his lifelong defense of the Prophet's hadith and his generous endowment of his wealth and library to the Muslim community.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Khatib's funeral procession proclaimed him as the one who defended the Prophet (peace be upon him). If your own life were announced in the same way, what would people say you stood for? What specific change can you make today to align your actions with that declaration?
?
He gave away all his wealth, even his clothes, while still alive. What attachment to material possessions is holding you back from true generosity? Will you identify one item this week to give away solely for Allah's sake, without expecting anything in return?
?
His legacy continues through his books and endowments. What legacy are you building right now—through your time, knowledge, or resources—that will benefit the Muslim community long after you are gone? Write down one concrete step you will take this month to create something lasting for the ummah.

The Life and Legacy of al-Khatib al-Baghdadi
Biographical notice on al-Khatib al-Baghdadi covering his death, birth, teachers, and works.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key biographical details of al-Khatib al-Baghdadi, including his death, his works, his teachers, and his theological affiliation.

Core Idea
Al-Khatib al-Baghdadi was a defender of the Prophet and a prolific scholar, buried near Ahmad ibn Hanbal yet an Ash'ari.

This passage from Ibn Asakir's Tabyin Kadhib al-Muftari presents a detailed biographical notice on the great hadith scholar al-Khatib al-Baghdadi. The account describes his funeral, his charitable acts, his vast output of works, and his teachers, concluding with praise of his scholarly qualities. It also clarifies his theological stance as an Ash'ari, which may surprise some given his burial near Ahmad ibn Hanbal.

Guided Path
1
Read the account of his death
Read the first part describing his death and funeral. Notice the eulogies shouted by the crowd, which highlight his role in defending the Prophet.
2
Identify his charitable actions
Find the sentence about his charity and endowment of his books. This shows his generosity and concern for knowledge.
3
Count his works and note his birth year
The passage gives the number of his works (56) and his birth year (391 or 392 AH). His magnum opus is Tarikh Baghdad in 106 volumes.
4
List his teachers and school
Identify the names of his teachers in hadith and jurisprudence. Note that he adhered to the Ash'ari school of theology.
5
Reflect on the overall portrait
Consider all the details: his death, charity, works, teachers, and creed. What kind of scholar was al-Khatib al-Baghdadi? How does this passage contribute to his legacy?

أبي الحسن الأشعري رحمه الله زادنا أبو محمد بن الاكفانى وكان قد رحل إلى نيسابور وأصبهان والبصرة وغيرها وكان مكثراً من الحديث عانياً بجمعه ثقة حافظاً متقناً متيقظاً متحمداً مصنفاً رحمه الله ورضى ورضى عنه .
I read in the handwriting of the trustworthy shaykh Abū al-Faḍl Aḥmad ibn al-Ḥasan ibn Khayrūn al-Bāqillānī in Baghdad in the year 463 AH: Abū Bakr Aḥmad ibn ʿAlī ibn Thābit ibn Aḥmad ibn Mahdī al-Khaṭīb al-Ḥāfiẓ died in the forenoon of Monday and was buried on Tuesday in Dhū al-Ḥijjah at Bāb Ḥarb next to Bishr ibn al-Ḥārith; prayer was performed over him in the Jāmiʿ al-Manṣūr, and the judge Abū al-Ḥusayn Muḥammad ibn ʿAlī al-Muhtadī billāh prayed over him. He gave in charity all his wealth, which was two hundred dinars, and distributed it among the ḥadīth scholars, jurists, and poor during his illness. He instructed that all his remaining clothes and other items be given in charity, and he endowed all his books for the Muslims. His funeral procession left from a room adjoining the Niẓāmiyya school on Nahr Muʿallā, followed by the jurists and a huge crowd. The bier was carried and crossed over the bridge, and was taken to Jāmiʿ al-Manṣūr. In front of the bier were a group calling out: "This is the one who defended the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace; this is the one who refuted lies against the Messenger of Allah; this is the one who preserved the ḥadīth of the Messenger of Allah." The bier was passed through al-Karkh with a huge crowd. The people gathered in Jāmiʿ al-Manṣūr, and all the jurists, scholars, and the chief of the nobles attended. A huge crowd followed the bier to Bāb Ḥarb. Several completions of the Qurʾān were recited at the grave. May Allah be pleased with him, forgive him, and join him with His righteous servants. For truly, the knowledge of ḥadīth and its memorization reached its pinnacle with him. He composed fifty-six works on the science of ḥadīth, among them "Tārīkh Baghdād" in one hundred and six parts. He was born in the year 391 AH. The trustworthy shaykh Abū Muḥammad Hibat Allāh ibn Aḥmad al-Akfānī informed us, saying: Abū Muḥammad ʿAbd al-ʿAzīz ibn Aḥmad al-Kattānī al-Ḥāfiẓ narrated to us, saying: Letters from a group of people in Baghdad arrived in Damascus, each one mentioning in his letter that the imam, the ḥāfiẓ Abū Bakr Aḥmad ibn ʿAlī ibn Thābit ibn Aḥmad ibn Mahdī al-Khaṭīb al-Baghdādī, may Allah have mercy on him, died on Monday forenoon, the seventh of Dhū al-Ḥijjah of the year 463 AH. He was taken on Tuesday to the western side and buried near the grave of Aḥmad ibn Ḥanbal, next to the grave of Bishr ibn al-Ḥārith, may Allah have mercy on them both. Among those who carried his bier was the jurist imam Abū Isḥāq Ibrāhīm ibn ʿAlī al-Shīrāzī. He had with him two hundred dinars, which he gave in charity during his illness, and they were exhausted at his death. He, may Allah have mercy on him, used to mention that he was born on Thursday, with six days remaining in Jumādā al-Ākhira of the year 392 AH, and that he began hearing ḥadīth at the age of twenty. His shaykh Abū al-Qāsim al-Azharī ʿUbayd Allāh ibn Aḥmad ibn ʿUthmān wrote from him in the year 412 AH, and his shaykh Abū Bakr Aḥmad ibn Muḥammad ibn Aḥmad ibn Ghālib al-Barqānī al-Khwārazmī al-Ḥāfiẓ wrote from him in the year 419 AH. He had studied jurisprudence under the judge Abū al-Ṭayyib Ṭāhir ibn ʿAbd Allāh al-Ṭabarī and Abū Naṣr ibn al-Ṣabbāgh, and he adhered to the school of Abū al-Ḥasan al-Ashʿarī, may Allah have mercy on him. Abū Muḥammad ibn al-Akfānī added: He had traveled to Naysābūr, Iṣfahān, al-Baṣra, and other places. He had many ḥadīths, was diligent in collecting them, trustworthy, a ḥāfiẓ, precise, vigilant, praiseworthy, and an author. May Allah have mercy on him and be pleased with him.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage is a biographical notice on the renowned ḥadīth scholar al-Khaṭīb al-Baghdādī. It begins by describing his death and burial, noting the place and the crowds, and includes the eulogies shouted at his funeral, highlighting his defense of the Prophet and his preservation of ḥadīth. The account then details his charitable acts: he gave away all his wealth, clothed goods, and endowed his books. It records the number of his works (fifty-six) and the size of his magnum opus 'Tārīkh Baghdād' (106 volumes). The text provides two separate narrations about his death date and confirms his birth in 391 AH (or 392 according to another account). It mentions his teachers, his study of jurisprudence, and his adherence to the Ashʿarī school of theology. The passage concludes with a description of his travels and his qualities as a ḥadīth scholar: he was trustworthy, precise, vigilant, and prolific. The commentary follows the order of the Arabic: first the death and funeral, then his charity, his works, then the second narration confirming details, his birth, teachers, and final praise.

Key Terms
الخطيب البغدادي
تاريخ بغداد
الحافظ
أبو الحسن الأشعري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Because al-Khatib al-Baghdadi was buried near Ahmad ibn Hanbal, some assume he was a Hanbali in theology.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that he adhered to the Ash'ari school of theology (مذهب أبي الحسن الأشعري), showing that burial near a Hanbali figure does not indicate theological affiliation.

Checkpoint
How many works did al-Khatib al-Baghdadi compose according to this passage?
A) 56
B) 106
C) 391
D) 463

Key Takeaway
Al-Khatib al-Baghdadi was a towering hadith scholar, author of fifty-six works, a defender of the Prophet, and an adherent of the Ash'ari school.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Khatib al-Baghdadi's funeral was marked by people crying out that he defended the Messenger of Allah. If your funeral were held today, what would people cry out about you? Does your life reflect that same defense? What one action will you take this week to more actively defend the Prophet's teachings?
?
He gave away all his wealth and even his clothes during his illness. What material possession are you clinging to that reveals a lack of trust in Allah's provision? Commit today to give away one item of value as an act of reliance on Allah.
?
He studied under great scholars and then authored fifty-six works to preserve knowledge. What knowledge have you received that you have not passed on? Who is one person you can teach a hadith or lesson to this month?

Biography of al-Qushayri
Biographical notice on al-Qushayri covering his teachers, visit to Baghdad, and date of birth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key details of al-Qushayri's life, including his teachers, his role as a preacher, and his dual expertise in Ash'ari theology and Shafi'i jurisprudence.

Core Idea
Al-Qushayri was a renowned Ash'ari theologian, Shafi'i jurist, and preacher.

This passage from Ibn 'Asakir's biographical dictionary introduces us to the scholar and preacher Abu al-Qasim al-Qushayri. It lists his teachers, describes his visit to Baghdad, and highlights his expertise in both Ash'ari theology and Shafi'i law. This brief notice establishes al-Qushayri as a major figure in the transmission of Sunni scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the isnad (chain of transmission) at the beginning.
2
Identify key biographical details
The passage gives al-Qushayri's full name, his teachers, his visit to Baghdad, his preaching style, his doctrinal affiliations, and his birth date. Find each of these elements.
3
Note his teachers and scholarly affiliations
The passage lists a number of notable teachers, including Ibn Furak and al-Hakim al-Bayyi'. It explicitly states that he followed the Ash'ari school in principles and the Shafi'i school in branches.
This shows his integration of theology and law.
4
Consider the classification remark
The author mentions that al-Qushayri should have been in the third class but was delayed due to his later death. Think about the significance of this classification system.
This reflects the biographical tradition of ranking scholars by generation.
5
Reflect on the significance
Al-Qushayri was not only a preacher but a scholar grounded in both usul (theology) and furu' (law). This balanced profile made him a key figure in the transmission of Sunni Islam.

ومنهم الأستاذ أبو القسم القشيري النيسابوري ثم الاستوائي أخبرنا الشيخان أبو الحسن على بن أحمد بن منصور وأبو منصور محمد ابن عبد الملك بن الحسن ، قالا قال لنا الشيخ أبو بكر أحمد بن على الحافظ : عبد الكريم بن هوازن بن عبد الملك بن طلحة بن محمد أبو القسم القشيري النيسابورى ، سمع أحمد بن محمد بن عمر الخفاف ، ومحمد بن أحمد بن عبدوس المزكي ، وأبا نعيم عبد الملك بن الحسن الاسفرايني وعبد الرحيم بن إبراهيم بن محمد المزكي ، ومحمد بن الحسن ابن فورك والحاكم أبا عبد الله بن البيع ومحمد بن الحسن العلوي وأبا عبد الرحمن السلمى ، وقدم علينا فى سنة ثمان وأربعين وأربعمائة ، وحدث ببغداد وكتبنا عنه وكان يعظ وكان حسن الموعظة مليح الإشارة ، وكان يعرف الأصول على مذهب الأشعرى والفروع على مذهب الشافعي ، سألت القشيري عن مولده فقال في ربيع الأول من سنة ست وسبعين وثلاثمائة ، كان ينبغي أن يكون في الطبقة الثالثة وإنما أخرته لتأخر وفاته . كتب إلى الشيخ أبو الحسن عبد الغافر بن إسماعيل الفارسي قال : عبد الكريم بن هوازن بن عبد الملك بن طلحة بن محمد القشيري أبو
And among them is the master Abū al-Qāsim al-Qushayrī al-Naysābūrī, then al-Ustawāʾī. The two shaykhs Abū al-Ḥasan ʿAlī ibn Aḥmad ibn Manṣūr and Abū Manṣūr Muḥammad ibn ʿAbd al-Malik ibn al-Ḥasan informed us, both saying: The shaykh Abū Bakr Aḥmad ibn ʿAlī al-Ḥāfiẓ narrated to us: ʿAbd al-Karīm ibn Hawāzin ibn ʿAbd al-Malik ibn Ṭalḥa ibn Muḥammad Abū al-Qāsim al-Qushayrī al-Naysābūrī heard from Aḥmad ibn Muḥammad ibn ʿUmar al-Khaffāf, and Muḥammad ibn Aḥmad ibn ʿAbdūs al-Muzakkī, and Abū Nuʿaym ʿAbd al-Malik ibn al-Ḥasan al-Isfarāʾīnī, and ʿAbd al-Raḥīm ibn Ibrāhīm ibn Muḥammad al-Muzakkī, and Muḥammad ibn al-Ḥasan ibn Fūrak, and al-Ḥākim Abū ʿAbd Allāh ibn al-Bayyiʿ, and Muḥammad ibn al-Ḥasan al-ʿAlawī, and Abū ʿAbd al-Raḥmān al-Sulamī. He came to us in the year 448 AH, and narrated ḥadīth in Baghdad, and we wrote from him. He used to preach, and his preaching was good and his gestures fine. He knew the principles (uṣūl) according to the school of al-Ashʿarī and the branches (furūʿ) according to the school of al-Shāfiʿī. I asked al-Qushayrī about his birth, and he said: 'In Rabīʿ al-Awwal of the year 376 AH.' He should have been in the third class, but I delayed him because of his death being later. The shaykh Abū al-Ḥasan ʿAbd al-Ghāfir ibn Ismāʿīl al-Fārisī wrote to me, saying: ʿAbd al-Karīm ibn Hawāzin ibn ʿAbd al-Malik ibn Ṭalḥa ibn Muḥammad al-Qushayrī Abū...
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage is a biographical notice on the scholar and preacher Abū al-Qāsim al-Qushayrī. It begins by listing his full name and his teachers, a long chain of notable scholars including Ibn Fūrak and al-Ḥākim al-Bayyiʿ. The text then recounts his arrival in Baghdad in 448 AH, where he narrated ḥadīth and preached, noted for his good preaching and fine gestures. It explicitly states that he knew the uṣūl (principles of religion) according to the Ashʿarī school and the furūʿ (branches of jurisprudence) according to the Shāfiʿī school. The passage then records his own statement about his birth date: Rabīʿ al-Awwal 376 AH. The narrator adds that he should have been placed in an earlier class of scholars (the third) but was delayed because of his later death. The text then begins a citation from ʿAbd al-Ghāfir al-Fārisī that repeats the name, but cuts off at the word 'Abū'. The commentary follows the order: naming, teachers, arrival, preaching, doctrinal affiliation, birth date, and classification note.

Correction: The passage explicitly states that he knew usul (principles) according to the Ash'ari school and furu' (branches) according to the Shafi'i school, demonstrating his solid grounding in both theology and law.

?

?

?
He traveled to Baghdad to teach. What sacrifice have you made for seeking or spreading knowledge? Are you content with staying comfortable?

Life and Legacy of Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi
Ibn Asakir records the birth, teachers, and death of the jurist Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life and scholarly profile of Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi as recorded by Ibn Asakir, including his birth, teachers, travels, and death.

Core Idea
Biographical notices preserve more than dates—they reveal character and scholarly legacy.

Ibn Asakir's Tabyin contains biographical entries that are not just dry lists but convey the piety and scholarship of the subject. In this lesson, we examine the entry on Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi, a prominent Shafi'i-Ash'ari jurist, and learn how to read such notices for historical and spiritual benefit.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the flow from mention of his teachers to his personal details.
2
Identify key facts
Extract the birth date, teachers, travels, and death mentioned. Also note the charity detail.
The birth is given as Thursday, 24 Jumada al-Akhirah 392 AH.
3
Reflect on the charity detail
Ask yourself what the detail about giving away all his money in charity during illness tells you about al-Shirazi's character.
This shows his detachment from worldly wealth.
4
Analyze the scholarly descriptions
Notice the words 'thiqah, hafizan, mutqinan, mutayaqqizan, mahmudan' and consider what each implies about his expertise.
These are technical terms of hadith criticism.
5
Consider the purpose
Think about why Ibn Asakir includes such biographical entries. What is the value of recording these details for future generations?
This preserves the chain of transmission and exemplifies good character.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حمهما الله ، وكان أحد من حمل جنازته الفقيه الإمام أبو إسحق إبراهيم ابن على الشيرازي وأنه كان معه ما يتا دينار فتصدق بها فى علته فانتهی فراغها بموته ، وكان رحمه الله يذكر أنه ولد يوم الخميس لست بقين من جمادى الآخرة من سنة أثنتين وتسعين وثلاثمائة وأنه أسمع الحديث وهو ابن عشرين سنة ، وكتب عنه شيخه أبو القسم الأزهرى عبيد الله بن أحمد بن عثمان في سنة اثنتى عشرة وكتب عنه شيخه أبو بكر أحمد بن محمد بن أحمد بن غالب البرقانی الخوارزمي الحافظ فى سنة تسع عشرة وأربعمائة، وكان قد علق الفقه عن القاضي أبي الطيب طاهر بن عبد الله الطبري وأبي نصر بن الصباغ وكان يذهب إلى مذهب أبي الحسن الأشعري رحمه الله زادنا أبو محمد بن الاكفانى وكان قد رحل إلى نيسابور وأصبهان والبصرة وغيرها وكان مكثراً من الحديث عانياً بجمعه ثقة حافظاً متقناً متيقظاً متحمداً مصنفاً رحمه الله ورضى ورضى عنه .
May God have mercy on both of them. He was one of those who carried the bier of the jurist, the Imam Abu Ishaq Ibrahim ibn Ali al-Shirazi, and that he had with him what [؟] dinar, and he gave them in charity during his illness, so its depletion ended with his death. He (may God have mercy on him) used to mention that he was born on Thursday with six nights remaining [literally: six remaining] of Jumada al-Akhirah of the year 392 AH, and that he heard hadith when he was twenty years old. His teacher Abu al-Qasim al-Azhari, Ubaydullah ibn Ahmad ibn Uthman, wrote from him in the year 412, and his teacher Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Ghalib al-Barqani al-Khwarizmi al-Hafiz wrote from him in the year 419. He had studied fiqh under al-Qadi Abu al-Tayyib Tahir ibn Abdullah al-Tabari and Abu Nasr ibn al-Sabbagh, and he followed the madhhab of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari (may God have mercy on him). Abu Muhammad ibn al-Akfani added [information] that he had traveled to Nishapur, Isfahan, Basra, and other places, and was abundant in hadith, diligent in collecting it, trustworthy, a hafiz, precise, vigilant, praiseworthy, an author. May God have mercy on him and be pleased with him.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage is a biographical notice by Ibn Asakir on the Shafi'i jurist Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi (d. 476 AH). It begins by stating that the author's two teachers (from the previous context) earned God's mercy, and then it mentions that one of them was among those who carried al-Shirazi's funeral bier. The text then notes that al-Shirazi had a sum of money (perhaps 'something like two dinars'?—the OCR is unclear) which he gave in charity during his illness, so that the money was exhausted at his death. His birth is recorded as Thursday, 24 Jumada al-Akhirah 392 AH. He began to hear hadith at age twenty. Teachers wrote from him in 412 and 419, indicating he himself transmitted hadith early. His fiqh teachers were al-Qadi Abu al-Tayyib al-Tabari and Abu Nasr ibn al-Sabbagh. He adhered to the Ash'ari madhhab. Ibn al-Akfani added that he traveled to major scholarly centers and was a prolific hadith scholar, trustworthy, a hafiz, precise, and an author. The notice concludes with a prayer for mercy.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Shirazi gave away his last coins during his final illness, leaving nothing behind. If you knew you would die in a week, what attachments would you still be clutching? Name them honestly, and ask yourself: do you trust Allah enough to let go even now?
?
He traveled to Nishapur, Isfahan, and Basra—hundreds of miles—seeking hadith. What discomfort or sacrifice have you made this month to learn your religion? Not what you planned, but what you actually did. If the answer is nothing, what will you change tomorrow?
?
The biographers called him 'precise, vigilant, praiseworthy'. Which of these three is missing from your relationship with the Qur'an and Sunnah? Write down one specific habit you will start this week to cultivate that trait.

Al-Qushayri: Lineage, Teachers, and Scholarly Identity
Ibn Asakir introduces al-Qushayri's lineage, teachers, and scholarly profile.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Qushayri's noble lineage, his key teachers, and his mastery of both Ash'ari theology and Shafi'i fiqh.

Core Idea
Al-Qushayri combined Ash'ari theology with Shafi'i fiqh and eloquent Sufi preaching.

This lesson introduces the renowned scholar Abu al-Qasim al-Qushayri through the biographical lens of Ibn Asakir. We learn about his Arab lineage from the Ustawa region, his study under the leading scholars of Khurasan, and his reputation as a preacher and master of the Islamic sciences. The passage establishes his unique position as a theologian, jurist, and spiritual guide.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Note how Ibn Asakir introduces al-Qushayri through an isnad (chain of transmission).
The isnad shows the reliability of the biography.
2
Identify al-Qushayri's teachers
List the eight teachers mentioned from whom he heard hadith. Recognize names like Ibn Furak and al-Hakim al-Naysaburi.
3
Reflect on his dual mastery
Notice that al-Qushayri knew usul on the Ash'ari madhhab and furu on the Shafi'i madhhab. Consider why this combination is significant.
This shows he was both a theologian and a jurist.

وكان حسن الموعظة مليح الإشارة ، وكان يعرف الأصول على مذهب الأشعرى والفروع على مذهب الشافعي ، سألت القشيري عن مولده فقال في ربيع الأول من سنة ست وسبعين ر ثلاثماية ، كان ينبغي أن يكون في الطبقة الثالثة وإنما أخرته لتأخر وفاته . كتب إلى الشيخ أبو الحسن عبد الغافر بن إسماعيل الفارسي قال : عبد الكريم بن هوازن بن عبد الملك بن طلحة بن محمد القشيري أبو القسم الإمام مطلقا الفقيه المتكلم الأصولى ، المفسر الأديب النحوى الله الكاتب الشاعر ، لسان عصره وسيد وقته وسر بين خلقه ، شیخ المشايخ وأستاذ الجماعة ومقدم الطائفة ومقصود سالكي الطريقة ، وبندار الحقيقة السعادة وقطب السيادة وحقيقة الملاحة لم ير مثل نفسه ، ولا رأى الراؤون مثله فى كماله وبراعته ، جمع من علم الشريعة والحقيقة وشرح أحسن الشرح أصول الطريقة ، أصله من ناحية استواء من العرب الذين وردوا خراسان وسكنوا النواحى فهو قشيرى الأب سلمى الأم وخاله أبو عقيل السلمي ، من وجوده دهاقين ناحية استواء توفى أبوه وهو طفل فوقع إلى أبى القسم الاليماني فقرأ الأدب والعربية عليه بسبب أتصاله بهم، وقرأ على غيره وحضر البلد واتفق حضوره مجلس الأستاذ الشهيد أبى على الحسن بن على الدقاق وكان لسان وقته فاستحسن كلامه وسلك طريق الارادة فقبله الأستاذ وأشار عليه بتعلم العلم ، فخرج إلى درس الشيخ الإمام أبي بكر محمد بن بكر الطوسى وشرع فى الفقه حتى فرغ من التعليق ثم اختلف باشاراته إلى الاستاذ الإمام أبي بكر ابن فورك وكان المقدم في الأصول حتى حصلها ، وبرع فيها وصار من أوجه تلامذته وأشدهم تحقيقاً وضبطا ، وقرأ عليه أصول الفقه وفرغ منه ، وبعد وفاة الأستاذ أبي بكر اختلف إلى الأستاذ أبى إسحق الاسفرايني وقعد يسمع جميع دروسه وأتى عليه أيام فقال له الأستاذ هذا العلم لا يحصل بالسماع وما توهم فيه ضبط ما يسمع ، فأعاد عنده ما سمعه منه وقرره أحسن تقرير من غير إخلال بشئ فتعجب منه وعرف محله وأكرمه وقال ما كنت أدرى أنك بلغت هذا المحل فلست تحتاج إلى درسى بل يكفيك أن تطالع مصنفاتى ، وتنظر فى طريقى وإن أشكل عليك شئ طالعتنى به ففعل ذلك وجمع بين طريقته وطريقة ابن فورك ثم نظر بعد ذلك في كتب القاضي أبي بكر بن الطيب وهو مع ذلك يحضر مجلس الأستاذ أبي على إلى أن أختاره لكريمته فزوجها منه وبعد وفاة الأستاذ عاشر أبا عبد الرحمن السلمي إلى أن صار أستاذ خراسان وأخذ فى التصنيف فصنف التفسير الكبير قبل العشر وأربعمائة ورتب المجالس وخرج إلى الحج في رفقة فـيـهـا الإمام أبو محمد الجويني والشيخ أحمد البيهقى وجماعة من المشاهير، فسمع معهم
And among them is the master Abu al-Qasim al-Qushayri al-Naysaburi, then al-Ustawai. Both Shaykhs Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Ahmad ibn Mansur and Abu Mansur Muhammad ibn Abd al-Malik ibn al-Hasan informed us, they said: Shaykh Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali al-Hafiz said to us: Abd al-Karim ibn Hawazin ibn Abd al-Malik ibn Talha ibn Muhammad Abu al-Qasim al-Qushayri al-Naysaburi. He heard from Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Umar al-Khaffaf, and Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Abdus al-Muzakki, and Abu Nuaym Abd al-Malik ibn al-Hasan al-Isfara'ini, and Abd al-Rahim ibn Ibrahim ibn Muhammad al-Muzakki, and Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn Furak, and al-Hakim Abu Abd Allah ibn al-Bayyi, and Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Alawi, and Abu Abd al-Rahman al-Sulami. He came to us in the year 448, and narrated hadith in Baghdad, and we wrote from him. He used to preach, and his preaching was good, and his allusions were beautiful. He knew the principles (usul) according to the Ash'ari madhhab and the branches (furu) according to the Shafi'i madhhab. I asked al-Qushayri about his birth, so he said: In Rabi' al-Awwal of the year 376. He should have been in the third class, but I delayed him because of the lateness of his death. Abu al-Hasan Abd al-Ghafir ibn Isma'il al-Farsi wrote to me, saying: Abd al-Karim ibn Hawazin ibn Abd al-Malik ibn Talha ibn Muhammad al-Qushayri, Abu al-Qasim, the absolute Imam, the jurist, the theologian, the usuli, the exegete, the litterateur, the grammarian, the [؟] writer, the poet, the tongue of his age, the master of his time, the secret among His creation, the shaykh of shaykhs, the teacher of the group, the foremost of the sect, the goal of the wayfarers of the path, the [؟] of truth, the happiness, the pole of sovereignty, the essence of grace – he has not seen the like of himself, nor have the seers seen his like in his perfection and brilliance. He combined the knowledge of Sharia and truth, and he explained in the best explanation the principles of the path. His origin is from the region of Ustawa, from among the Arabs who came to Khurasan and settled in those districts. So he is Qushayri on his father's side, Sulami on his mother's side, and his maternal uncle is Abu Aqil al-Sulami. From his generosity [؟] the landlords of the region of Ustawa. His father died when he was a child, so he fell to Abu al-Qasim al-Yamani [؟], and he read literature and Arabic under him due to his connection with them. He also read under others. He attended the city, and it happened that he attended the circle of the martyred master Abu Ali al-Hasan ibn Ali al-Daqqaq, who was the tongue of his time. He admired his speech and followed the path of desire [؟], so the master accepted him and advised him to learn knowledge. So he went out to the lessons of Shaykh Imam Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Bakr al-Tusi and began fiqh until he finished the commentary. Then, by his indications [؟], he frequented the master Imam Abu Bakr ibn Furak, who was the foremost in principles (usul) until he mastered them, and excelled in them, and became one of his most prominent students, and the most rigorous in verification and precise memorization. He read usul al-fiqh under him and completed it. After the death of master Abu Bakr, he frequented the master Abu Ishaq al-Isfara'ini and sat to listen to all his lessons. Some days passed, then the master said to him: 'This knowledge is not acquired by mere listening, and I doubt that you can accurately retain what you hear.' So he recited back to him what he had heard from him and articulated it in the best articulation without any omission. The master was amazed at him, recognized his standing, honored him, and said: 'I did not know that you had reached this level. You do not need my lesson; rather, it suffices for you to study my works and examine my method, and if something is unclear to you, you may consult me about it.' He did that, and he combined his method with the method of Ibn Furak. Then after that he examined the books of Qadi Abu Bakr ibn al-Tayyib. Meanwhile, he continued to attend the circle of master Abu Ali until he chose him for his honorable daughter [lit. 'for his generous one'] and married her to him. After the death of the master, he kept company with Abu Abd al-Rahman al-Sulami until he became the master of Khurasan. He began authoring, so he authored the Great Tafsir before the year 410. He organized sessions, and set out for Hajj in a group that included Imam Abu Muhammad al-Juwayni, Shaykh Ahmad al-Bayhaqi, and a group of notable figures. He listened [to hadith] with them.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage is a lengthy biographical notice on Abu al-Qasim al-Qushayri (d. 465 AH), one of the most important figures in Ash'ari kalam, Shafi'i fiqh, and Sufism. Ibn Asakir begins with his chain of transmission, then names the shaykhs from whom al-Qushayri heard hadith, including many well-known scholars like Ibn Furak and al-Hakim al-Naysaburi. He states that al-Qushayri came to Baghdad in 448 AH, preached eloquently, and knew usul (theology/jurisprudence) on the Ash'ari madhhab and furu on the Shafi'i madhhab. His birth year is given as 376 AH. The author notes that al-Qushayri should have been placed in an earlier 'class' of hadith transmitters but was delayed due to his later death. A letter from Abd al-Ghafir al-Farsi praises al-Qushayri with superlatives, calling him the 'absolute Imam,' a theologian, usuli, exegete, poet, etc., and emphasizing his unmatched perfection. Then the text turns to his lineage: he is of Arab origin from the Ustawa region, with both Qushayri and Sulami tribal connections. His father died when he was young, so he was raised by Abu al-Qasim al-Yamani, under whom he studied literature and Arabic. He later attended the circle of the Sufi master Abu Ali al-Daqqaq, who recognized his talent and guided him toward learning. Al-Qushayri then studied fiqh under Abu Bakr al-Tusi, completed his commentary, and then moved on to study kalam (usul) under Abu Bakr ibn Furak, becoming his foremost student. After Ibn Furak's death, he studied under Abu Ishaq al-Isfara'ini, who initially doubted his listening ability but was astonished when al-Qushayri reproduced his lessons perfectly. Al-Isfara'ini then advised him to study his works independently. Al-Qushayri combined the methods of his teachers, also studied the works of Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani, and married the daughter of his earlier teacher Abu Ali al-Daqqaq. He later associated with the Sufi Abu Abd al-Rahman al-Sulami until he became the foremost scholar of Khurasan. He authored the Great Tafsir before 410 AH, organized teaching sessions, and went to Hajj with prominent scholars like al-Juwayni and al-Bayhaqi, listening to hadith with them. This biography highlights al-Qushayri's comprehensive mastery of both exoteric (Sharia) and esoteric (truth) sciences, his role as a bridge between kalam and Sufism, and his high status among the Ash'ari Shafi'i scholars.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That al-Qushayri was only a Sufi and not a theologian or jurist.
Correction: The passage clearly states he knew usul on the Ash'ari madhhab and furu on the Shafi'i madhhab, showing his mastery in both theology and law.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which two madhhabs did al-Qushayri master?
A) Hanafi and Ash'ari
B) Shafi'i and Ash'ari
C) Maliki and Ash'ari
D) Shafi'i and Hanbali

Key Takeaway
Al-Qushayri was a master of both Ash'ari theology and Shafi'i jurisprudence, equally respected as a preacher and scholar.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Qushayri mastered both principles and branches. In your own pursuit of knowledge, are you neglecting either the foundational principles or the practical applications? Which one do you tend to ignore, and what will you do to restore balance starting today?
?
The passage notes that al-Qushayri's preaching was 'good' and his allusions 'beautiful'. When you speak about Islam, do you seek to combine sound knowledge with beautiful presentation? What is one step you can take this week to improve either your knowledge or your delivery?
?
Al-Qushayri was described as knowing both usul and furu. Do you see yourself as someone who seeks comprehensive understanding, or do you prefer to focus on one area? How might this affect your ability to guide others, and what concrete change can you make to become more well-rounded?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
intermediate
6 min
The Educational Journey of al-Qushayri
Ibn Asakir details al-Qushayri's comprehensive education and his teachers' recognition of his genius.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Qushayri’s education under key Ash'ari and Shafi'i masters shaped his scholarly identity.

Core Idea
Al-Qushayri mastered both exoteric and esoteric sciences through a diverse education.

This lesson traces al-Qushayri’s transformation from a young orphan into the foremost scholar of Khurasan. We see his early training in Arabic, his turn to Sufism under al-Daqqaq, his methodical study of fiqh under al-Tusi, and his deep grounding in kalam under Ibn Furak and al-Isfara'ini. The passage highlights his intellectual rigor and his ability to synthesize different scholarly traditions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation, focusing on the sequence of teachers and subjects.
Pay attention to the test by al-Isfara'ini.
2
Map the educational stages
Identify each teacher and what al-Qushayri studied under them: al-Yamani (Arabic), al-Daqqaq (Sufism), al-Tusi (fiqh), Ibn Furak (kalam), al-Isfara'ini (kalam).
3
Understand the test
Al-Isfara'ini doubted al-Qushayri's learning ability, but al-Qushayri recited back perfectly, earning the teacher's respect and advice.
This shows al-Qushayri's exceptional memory and understanding.

You do not need my lesson; rather, it suffices for you to study my works and examine my method, and if something is unclear to you, you may consult me about it.' He did that, and he combined his method with the method of Ibn Furak. Then after that he examined the books of Qadi Abu Bakr ibn al-Tayyib. Commentary
This passage is a lengthy biographical notice on Abu al-Qasim al-Qushayri (d. 465 AH), one of the most important figures in Ash'ari kalam, Shafi'i fiqh, and Sufism. Ibn Asakir begins with his chain of transmission, then names the shaykhs from whom al-Qushayri heard hadith, including many well-known scholars like Ibn Furak and al-Hakim al-Naysaburi. He states that al-Qushayri came to Baghdad in 448 AH, preached eloquently, and knew usul (theology/jurisprudence) on the Ash'ari madhhab and furu on the Shafi'i madhhab. His birth year is given as 376 AH. The author notes that al-Qushayri should have been placed in an earlier 'class' of hadith transmitters but was delayed due to his later death. A letter from Abd al-Ghafir al-Farsi praises al-Qushayri with superlatives, calling him the 'absolute Imam,' a theologian, usuli, exegete, poet, etc., and emphasizing his unmatched perfection. Then the text turns to his lineage: he is of Arab origin from the Ustawa region, with both Qushayri and Sulami tribal connections. His father died when he was young, so he was raised by Abu al-Qasim al-Yamani, under whom he studied literature and Arabic. He later attended the circle of the Sufi master Abu Ali al-Daqqaq, who recognized his talent and guided him toward learning. Al-Qushayri then studied fiqh under Abu Bakr al-Tusi, completed his commentary, and then moved on to study kalam (usul) under Abu Bakr ibn Furak, becoming his foremost student. After Ibn Furak's death, he studied under Abu Ishaq al-Isfara'ini, who initially doubted his listening ability but was astonished when al-Qushayri reproduced his lessons perfectly. Al-Isfara'ini then advised him to study his works independently. Al-Qushayri combined the methods of his teachers, also studied the works of Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani, and married the daughter of his earlier teacher Abu Ali al-Daqqaq. He later associated with the Sufi Abu Abd al-Rahman al-Sulami until he became the foremost scholar of Khurasan. He authored the Great Tafsir before 410 AH, organized teaching sessions, and went to Hajj with prominent scholars like al-Juwayni and al-Bayhaqi, listening to hadith with them. This biography highlights al-Qushayri's comprehensive mastery of both exoteric (Sharia) and esoteric (truth) sciences, his role as a bridge between kalam and Sufism, and his high status among the Ash'ari Shafi'i scholars.

Key Terms
ابن فورك
أبو إسحق الإسفرايني
أبو علي الدقاق
المتكلم
الأصولي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That al-Qushayri was merely a Sufi without rigorous training in law and theology.
Correction: The passage details his systematic study of fiqh under al-Tusi and kalam under Ibn Furak and al-Isfara'ini, proving his deep academic training.

Checkpoint

B) Abu Ishaq al-Isfara'ini
C) Abu Ali al-Daqqaq
D) Abu Abd al-Rahman al-Sulami

Key Takeaway
Al-Qushayri's education combined spiritual training, jurisprudence, and theology, making him a comprehensive scholar.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When al-Isfara'ini doubted al-Qushayri's ability to learn by listening, al-Qushayri recited the entire lesson perfectly from memory. Have you ever been tested or doubted, and did you respond with humility and preparation? What would it take for you to be ready to prove your understanding under pressure?
?
Al-Qushayri combined the methods of Ibn Furak and al-Isfara'ini, not clinging to one teacher. Are you open to learning from different sources of knowledge, or do you limit yourself to one perspective? How can you actively integrate diverse teachings into your own understanding?
?
Al-Qushayri's spiritual training under al-Daqqaq preceded and accompanied his formal studies. Do you prioritize shaping your soul alongside acquiring knowledge? What one change could you make to ensure that your learning draws you closer to Allah rather than inflating your ego?

Al-Qushayri's Later Career and Legacy
Ibn Asakir concludes with al-Qushayri's scholarly output and his Hajj journey with prominent peers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Qushayri’s achievements as a teacher, author, and the leading figure of Khurasan.

Core Idea
Al-Qushayri wrote the Great Tafsir, led scholarly circles, and performed Hajj with leading scholars.

The final portion of Ibn Asakir's biography describes al-Qushayri’s post-education career. After his teachers passed away, he associated with the Sufi master al-Sulami and became the leading scholar of Khurasan. He authored his famous Great Tafsir before 410 AH, organized teaching sessions, and traveled for Hajj in the company of illustrious scholars like al-Juwayni and al-Bayhaqi. This lesson highlights his lasting contributions.

3

His Hajj journey with al-Juwayni and al-Bayhaqi indicates his high status.
