And among them is the master Abu al-Qasim al-Qushayri al-Naysaburi, then al-Ustawai. Both Shaykhs Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Ahmad ibn Mansur and Abu Mansur Muhammad ibn Abd al-Malik ibn al-Hasan informed us, they said: Shaykh Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali al-Hafiz said to us: Abd al-Karim ibn Hawazin ibn Abd al-Malik ibn Talha ibn Muhammad Abu al-Qasim al-Qushayri al-Naysaburi. He heard from Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Umar al-Khaffaf, and Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Abdus al-Muzakki, and Abu Nuaym Abd al-Malik ibn al-Hasan al-Isfara'ini, and Abd al-Rahim ibn Ibrahim ibn Muhammad al-Muzakki, and Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn Furak, and al-Hakim Abu Abd Allah ibn al-Bayyi, and Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Alawi, and Abu Abd al-Rahman al-Sulami. He came to us in the year 448, and narrated hadith in Baghdad, and we wrote from him. He used to preach, and his preaching was good, and his allusions were beautiful. He knew the principles (usul) according to the Ash'ari madhhab and the branches (furu) according to the Shafi'i madhhab. I asked al-Qushayri about his birth, so he said: In Rabi' al-Awwal of the year 376. He should have been in the third class, but I delayed him because of the lateness of his death. Abu al-Hasan Abd al-Ghafir ibn Isma'il al-Farsi wrote to me, saying: Abd al-Karim ibn Hawazin ibn Abd al-Malik ibn Talha ibn Muhammad al-Qushayri, Abu al-Qasim, the absolute Imam, the jurist, the theologian, the usuli, the exegete, the litterateur, the grammarian, the [؟] writer, the poet, the tongue of his age, the master of his time, the secret among His creation, the shaykh of shaykhs, the teacher of the group, the foremost of the sect, the goal of the wayfarers of the path, the [؟] of truth, the happiness, the pole of sovereignty, the essence of grace – he has not seen the like of himself, nor have the seers seen his like in his perfection and brilliance. He combined the knowledge of Sharia and truth, and he explained in the best explanation the principles of the path. His origin is from the region of Ustawa, from among the Arabs who came to Khurasan and settled in those districts. So he is Qushayri on his father's side, Sulami on his mother's side, and his maternal uncle is Abu Aqil al-Sulami. From his generosity [؟] the landlords of the region of Ustawa. His father died when he was a child, so he fell to Abu al-Qasim al-Yamani [؟], and he read literature and Arabic under him due to his connection with them. He also read under others. He attended the city, and it happened that he attended the circle of the martyred master Abu Ali al-Hasan ibn Ali al-Daqqaq, who was the tongue of his time. He admired his speech and followed the path of desire [؟], so the master accepted him and advised him to learn knowledge. So he went out to the lessons of Shaykh Imam Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Bakr al-Tusi and began fiqh until he finished the commentary. Then, by his indications [؟], he frequented the master Imam Abu Bakr ibn Furak, who was the foremost in principles (usul) until he mastered them, and excelled in them, and became one of his most prominent students, and the most rigorous in verification and precise memorization. He read usul al-fiqh under him and completed it. After the death of master Abu Bakr, he frequented the master Abu Ishaq al-Isfara'ini and sat to listen to all his lessons. Some days passed, then the master said to him: 'This knowledge is not acquired by mere listening, and I doubt that you can accurately retain what you hear.' So he recited back to him what he had heard from him and articulated it in the best articulation without any omission. The master was amazed at him, recognized his standing, honored him, and said: 'I did not know that you had reached this level. You do not need my lesson; rather, it suffices for you to study my works and examine my method, and if something is unclear to you, you may consult me about it.' He did that, and he combined his method with the method of Ibn Furak. Then after that he examined the books of Qadi Abu Bakr ibn al-Tayyib. Meanwhile, he continued to attend the circle of master Abu Ali until he chose him for his honorable daughter [lit. 'for his generous one'] and married her to him. After the death of the master, he kept company with Abu Abd al-Rahman al-Sulami until he became the master of Khurasan. He began authoring, so he authored the Great Tafsir before the year 410. He organized sessions, and set out for Hajj in a group that included Imam Abu Muhammad al-Juwayni, Shaykh Ahmad al-Bayhaqi, and a group of notable figures. He listened [to hadith] with them.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage is a lengthy biographical notice on Abu al-Qasim al-Qushayri (d. 465 AH), one of the most important figures in Ash'ari kalam, Shafi'i fiqh, and Sufism. Ibn Asakir begins with his chain of transmission, then names the shaykhs from whom al-Qushayri heard hadith, including many well-known scholars like Ibn Furak and al-Hakim al-Naysaburi. He states that al-Qushayri came to Baghdad in 448 AH, preached eloquently, and knew usul (theology/jurisprudence) on the Ash'ari madhhab and furu on the Shafi'i madhhab. His birth year is given as 376 AH. The author notes that al-Qushayri should have been placed in an earlier 'class' of hadith transmitters but was delayed due to his later death. A letter from Abd al-Ghafir al-Farsi praises al-Qushayri with superlatives, calling him the 'absolute Imam,' a theologian, usuli, exegete, poet, etc., and emphasizing his unmatched perfection. Then the text turns to his lineage: he is of Arab origin from the Ustawa region, with both Qushayri and Sulami tribal connections. His father died when he was young, so he was raised by Abu al-Qasim al-Yamani, under whom he studied literature and Arabic. He later attended the circle of the Sufi master Abu Ali al-Daqqaq, who recognized his talent and guided him toward learning. Al-Qushayri then studied fiqh under Abu Bakr al-Tusi, completed his commentary, and then moved on to study kalam (usul) under Abu Bakr ibn Furak, becoming his foremost student. After Ibn Furak's death, he studied under Abu Ishaq al-Isfara'ini, who initially doubted his listening ability but was astonished when al-Qushayri reproduced his lessons perfectly. Al-Isfara'ini then advised him to study his works independently. Al-Qushayri combined the methods of his teachers, also studied the works of Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani, and married the daughter of his earlier teacher Abu Ali al-Daqqaq. He later associated with the Sufi Abu Abd al-Rahman al-Sulami until he became the foremost scholar of Khurasan. He authored the Great Tafsir before 410 AH, organized teaching sessions, and went to Hajj with prominent scholars like al-Juwayni and al-Bayhaqi, listening to hadith with them. This biography highlights al-Qushayri's comprehensive mastery of both exoteric (Sharia) and esoteric (truth) sciences, his role as a bridge between kalam and Sufism, and his high status among the Ash'ari Shafi'i scholars.

Misconception: That al-Qushayri’s tafsir was his only major work; the passage shows he also taught and organized sessions.
Correction: The passage clearly states he 'organized sessions' (ratta al-majalis) and was a teacher, in addition to authoring the Tafsir.

The Scholar's Titles and Lineage
Ibn Asakir enumerates the scholar's titles and establishes his lineage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how traditional Islamic biographers used honorific titles to convey a scholar's comprehensive mastery and noble lineage.

Core Idea
A scholar's titles reveal his mastery across many sciences and his noble heritage.

Ibn Asakir opens his biographical entry with a cascade of honorifics. These are not mere flattery—they serve to position the scholar within the intellectual and spiritual genealogy of Islamic learning. By reading this passage, we learn how medieval scholars presented a person's credentials through a combination of academic achievements and tribal lineage.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic once, then the English. Notice the rhythm of the accolades.
2
Identify the disciplines listed
The passage mentions fiqh, kalam, usul, tafsir, adab, nahw, kitaba, shi'r. Count them.
There are at least eight.
3
Examine the lineage statements
The passage tells us the scholar's father was Qushayri, mother Sulami, and his maternal uncle was Abu Aqil al-Sulami. This shows the importance of both tribal and scholarly descent.

وعين القسم الإمام مطلقا الفقيه المتكلم الأصولى، المفسر الأديب النحوى الله الكاتب الشاعر، لسان عصره وسيد وقته وسر بين خلقه، شیخ المشايخ وأستاذ الجماعة ومقدم الطائفة ومقصوصدي سالكي الطريقة، وبندار الحقيقة السعادة وقطب السيادة وحقيقة الملاحة لم ير مثل نفسه، ولا رأى الراؤون مثله فى كماله وبراعته، جمع من علم الشريعة والحقيقة وشرح أحسن الشرح أصول الطريقة، أصله من ناحية استواء من العرب الذين وردوا خراسان وسكنوا النواحى فهو قشيرى الأب سلمى الأم وخاله أبو عقيل السلمي.
And distinguished [is] the Imam absolutely, the jurist, the theologian, the fundamentalist, the exegete, the literary man, the grammarian, [the scribe?] of Allah, the writer, the poet, the tongue of his age, the master of his time, the secret among His creation, the shaykh of shaykhs, the teacher of the group, the foremost of the community, the desire of the seekers of the path, the chief of truth and happiness, the pole of lordship and the essence of grace – no one like himself was seen, nor did the seers see his like in his perfection and brilliance. He combined the sciences of the Law and the Truth, and explained the principles of the path in the best explanation. His origin was from the district of Istawa, from among the Arabs who came to Khurasan and settled in those regions; he is Qushayri on the father's side and Sulami on the mother's side, and his maternal uncle is Abu Aqil al-Sulami.

Commentary
This passage is an introduction to the biography, praising the scholar with a series of honorific titles. The author, Ibn Asakir, begins by listing the many disciplines the scholar mastered: jurisprudence (fiqh), theology (kalam), usul al-fiqh, tafsir, literature, grammar, writing, and poetry. He then calls him the 'tongue of his age' and the 'master of his time', emphasizing his unique status. The passage then clarifies his lineage: he comes from the district of Istawa in Khurasan, from Arab stock. His father was from the Qushayr tribe, and his mother from the Sulaym tribe; her brother was Abu Aqil al-Sulami. This establishes his noble Arab and scholarly heritage.

?

What will you do to ensure you are part of an unbroken line of knowledge?
?
The passage says 'no one like himself was seen' and 'nor did the seers see his like in his perfection and brilliance.' Do you ever feel a sting of mediocrity when you compare your own output – your memorization, your understanding, your character – to such a description? Instead of feeling defeated, ask yourself: what is the one area of knowledge where you can strive for excellence starting tomorrow? Name it.

Early Education and Teachers
Details the scholar's early studies and his teachers' guidance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholar's educational journey, highlighting the importance of active engagement and mastery in acquiring knowledge.

Core Idea
True learning requires active engagement, not passive listening.

This passage narrates the early education of a prominent scholar, tracing his studies from Arabic literature to fiqh and usul. It illustrates how his dedication and intellectual rigor earned him the recognition of his teachers, culminating in a powerful lesson about the nature of knowledge acquisition.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Focus on the sequence of teachers and subjects the scholar studied.
Notice the scholar's transition from literature to fiqh to usul.
2
Identify the teachers and subjects
List the teachers mentioned: Abu al-Qasim al-Alimani (literature), Abu Ali al-Daqqaq (spiritual guidance), Abu Bakr al-Tusi (fiqh), Ibn Furak (usul), Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini (usul).
Each teacher played a specific role in his development.
3
Analyze the turning point with al-Isfarayini
Notice how al-Isfarayini initially doubted the scholar's ability to learn by hearing alone, and how the scholar proved his mastery by reproducing the lessons perfectly.
This demonstrates the difference between passive listening and active understanding.
4
Reflect on the deeper lesson
Consider what this passage teaches about the nature of knowledge acquisition. The scholar did not just attend lectures; he internalized and could reproduce the material.
This connects to the core idea of active engagement.

من وجوده دهاقين ناحية استواء توفى أبوه وهو طفل فوقع إلى أبى القسم الاليماني فقرأ الأدب والعربية عليه بسبب أتصاله بهم، وقرأ على غيره وحضر البلد واتفق حضوره مجلس الأستاذ الشهيد أبى على الحسن بن على الدقاق وكان لسان وقته فاستحسن كلامه وسلك طريق الارادة فقبله الأستاذ وأشار عليه بتعلم العلم، فخرج إلى درس الشيخ الإمام أبي بكر محمد بن بكر الطوسى وشرع فى الفقه حتى فرغ من التعليق ثم اختلف باشاراته إلى الاستاذ الإمام أبي بكر ابن فورك وكان المقدم في الأصول حتى حصلها، وبرع فيها وصار من أوجه تلامذته وأشدهم تحقيقاً وضبطا، وقرأ عليه أصول الفقه وفرغ منه، وبعد وفاة الأستاذ أبي بكر اختلف إلى الأستاذ أبى إسحق الاسفرايني وقعد يسمع جميع دروسه وأتى عليه أيام فقال له الأستاذ هذا العلم لا يحصل بالسماع وما توهم فيه ضبط ما يسمع، فأعاد عنده ما سمعه منه وقرره أحسن تقرير من غير إخلال بشئ فتعجب منه وعرف محله وأكرمه وقال ما كنت أدرى أنك بلغت هذا المحل فلست تحتاج إلى درسى بل يكفيك أن تطالع مصنفاتى، وتنظر فى طريقى إن أشكل عليك شئ طالعتنى به.
From his existence [as] a peasant? of the district of Istawa, his father died while he was a child, so he fell to Abu al-Qasim al-Alimani and read literature and Arabic upon him due to his connection with them. He also read upon others and came to the city, and it happened that he attended the assembly of the martyr master Abu Ali al-Hasan ibn Ali al-Daqqaq, who was the tongue of his time. He admired his speech and followed the path of spiritual desire, so the master accepted him and advised him to learn knowledge. So he went out to the lesson of Shaykh Imam Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Bakr al-Tusi and began in fiqh until he finished the teaching commentary. Then he frequented with his signs to the master Imam Abu Bakr ibn Furak, who was the foremost in usul until he acquired it, and excelled in it, and became one of his foremost students and the most thorough and precise among them. He read upon him usul al-fiqh and completed it. After the death of master Abu Bakr, he frequented to master Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini and sat listening to all his lessons, and some days passed upon him. So the master said to him: 'This knowledge is not acquired by hearing, and you imagine that you can grasp what you hear?' So he repeated before him what he had heard from him and presented it in the best presentation without any omission, so he (Abu Ishaq) marveled at him, recognized his worth, honored him, and said: 'I did not know that you had reached this level. You do not need my lesson; rather it suffices you to study my works and look into my method. If something is difficult for you, come to me with it.'
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage narrates the scholar's educational journey. After his father's death, he came under the care of Abu al-Qasim al-Alimani, with whom he studied Arabic literature. He also studied with others and eventually attended the gathering of Abu Ali al-Daqqaq, a prominent spiritual master. Al-Daqqaq recognized his potential and encouraged him to pursue formal Islamic sciences. He then began studying fiqh under Abu Bakr al-Tusi. After that, he studied usul al-din (theology) under Abu Bakr ibn Furak, becoming one of his top students. Following Ibn Furak's death, he attended the lessons of Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini. Initially al-Isfarayini doubted that the scholar could learn by mere listening, but the scholar demonstrated his mastery by perfectly reproducing what he had heard, impressing his teacher. Al-Isfarayini then told him that he no longer needed to attend his lessons but could study his works directly.

Key Terms
الأدب
الفقه
الأصول
ابن فورك
الاسفرايني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Knowledge can be acquired by passive listening alone.
Correction: The scholar proved that mastery requires active engagement and demonstration of understanding; his teacher al-Isfarayini explicitly said 'this knowledge is not acquired by hearing.'

Checkpoint
Why did Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini initially doubt the scholar's ability to learn?
A) Because the scholar was too young
B) Because al-Isfarayini believed knowledge cannot be acquired by hearing alone
C) Because the scholar had not studied fiqh
D) Because the scholar was from a different region

Key Takeaway
This passage teaches that true mastery comes from active engagement and the ability to demonstrate one's understanding, not just passive attendance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sit in a lecture or read a book, do you expect to learn just by being present? When was the last time you forced yourself to reproduce what you heard without any notes, and how did that change your understanding? What will you do this week to move from passive listening to active engagement?
?
The scholar mastered his subjects to the point that his teacher said, 'I did not know that you had reached this level.' What area of your deen are you content with mere exposure, not mastery? What would it take for a teacher to say that about you?
?
Abu Ishaq initially doubted the scholar's ability, but the scholar proved him by perfectly repeating and explaining the lessons. Who might be doubting your commitment to learning—and are you proving them wrong by your active effort, or are you content to let their doubts remain justified?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir

Al-Qushayri's Synthesis, Marriage, and Authorship
Biographical narrative of al-Qushayri's synthesis, marriage, and early authorship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Qushayri synthesized the methods of Ibn Furak and al-Isfarayini, married into a Sufi family, and composed his Great Tafsir early in his career.

Core Idea
Al-Qushayri's greatness came from synthesizing scholarly methods, spiritual mentorship, and early authorship.

This passage from Ibn Asakir's Tabyin Kidhb al-Muftari traces pivotal moments in Imam al-Qushayri's life: his intellectual synthesis of two great kalam masters, his marriage to the daughter of his Sufi master, and his early composition of the monumental Tafsir al-Kabir. It illustrates how traditional learning, spiritual companionship, and scholarly output intertwined in classical Islamic education.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage for sequence
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice the chronological flow: study, synthesis, marriage, association, authorship, Hajj.
2
Identify the two methods combined
The passage says he combined 'his method and the method of Ibn Furak'. Who are 'his' and Ibn Furak? 'His' refers to al-Isfarayini, whose method al-Qushayri synthesized with Ibn Furak's.
This synthesis is a hallmark of al-Qushayri's approach.
3
Trace the personal milestones
Note the marriage to Abu Ali al-Daqqaq's daughter, then after al-Daqqaq's death, association with Abu Abd al-Rahman al-Sulami, eventually becoming master of Khurasan.
These relationships show the integration of kalam and tasawwuf.
4
Reflect on the timeline of authorship
He wrote Tafsir al-Kabir before 410 AH (c. 1019 CE) – early in his career. That challenges the assumption that great works are only produced in old age.
Also note he organized gatherings and performed Hajj with famous scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ففعل ذلك وجمع بين طريقته وطريقة ابن فورك ثم نظر بعد ذلك في كتب القاضي أبي بكر بن الطيب وهو مع ذلك يحضر مجلس الأستاذ أبي على إلى أن أختاره لكريمته فزوجها منه وبعد وفاة الأستاذ عاشر أبا عبد الرحمن السلمي إلى أن صار أستاذ خراسان وأخذ فى التصنيف فصنف التفسير الكبير قبل العشر وأربعمائة ورتب المجالس وخرج إلى الحج في رفقة فيها الإمام أبو محمد الجويني والشيخ أحمد البيهقى وجماعة من المشاهير.
So he did that and combined between his method and the method of Ibn Furak. Then after that he looked into the books of Qadi Abu Bakr ibn al-Tayyib, while he also attended the assembly of master Abu Ali until he (Abu Ali) chose him for his noble daughter and married her to him. After the death of the master, he associated with Abu Abd al-Rahman al-Sulami until he became the master of Khurasan, and he began authoring. He composed the Great Tafsir before [the year] ten and four hundred (410 AH), and organized the gatherings, and went out for Hajj in a group that included Imam Abu Muhammad al-Juwayni and Shaykh Ahmad al-Bayhaqi and a group of well-known figures.
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage tells how the scholar implemented the advice of al-Isfarayini: he studied both his method and that of Ibn Furak, synthesizing them. He also studied the works of Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani (Ibn al-Tayyib). Meanwhile, he continued attending the gatherings of his spiritual master Abu Ali al-Daqqaq, who was so impressed that he chose him as a son-in-law. After al-Daqqaq's death, he associated with the Sufi master Abu Abd al-Rahman al-Sulami, eventually becoming the leading scholar of Khurasan. He then started writing, composing his famous 'Great Tafsir' before the year 410 AH (around 1019 CE). He also organized teaching sessions and performed Hajj in the company of notable scholars like al-Juwayni and al-Bayhaqi.

Key Terms
التفسير الكبير
القاضي أبو بكر بن الطيب
أبو عبد الرحمن السلمي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Tafsir al-Kabir was written in al-Qushayri's old age.
Correction: The text states it was composed before 410 AH, likely when he was in his 30s or 40s, showing his early scholarly output.

Checkpoint
What was the name of the tafsir that al-Qushayri composed before 410 AH?
A) Tafsir al-Jalalayn
B) Tafsir al-Kabir
C) Tafsir al-Bayhaqi
D) Tafsir al-Juwayni

Key Takeaway
Al-Qushayri's synthesis of kalam and Sufi traditions, along with his early authorship of Tafsir al-Kabir, established him as a leading scholar of Khurasan before 410 AH.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Qushayri invested time in multiple scholars and synthesized their methods. Are you willing to step out of your comfort zone to learn from those with different approaches to faith, even if it challenges your current understanding? What is one concrete step you can take this week to seek knowledge from a source you have avoided?
?
He began authoring his great tafsir early in his career, before age 40. What is one project for the sake of your deen that you have been putting off, telling yourself you are not ready? What would it look like to start, even imperfectly, this very week?
?
Al-Qushayri's consistency in attending his teacher's gatherings led to being chosen as a son-in-law and eventually becoming the master of Khurasan. Are you part of a learning circle or spiritual community that you attend with such dedication? If not, what is the real reason you hesitate? If yes, how can you deepen that commitment starting today?

Hadith Studies in Baghdad and the Hijaz
Biographical mention of hadith studies in Baghdad and Hijaz.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholar's hadith studies and his travels to Baghdad and the Hijaz to learn from shaykhs.

Core Idea
The scholar's journey combined hadith study with physical arts.

This passage introduces the scholar's early hadith education. During his travels, he heard hadith from prominent shaykhs in Baghdad and the Hijaz. This laid the foundation for his later mastery.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic sentence
Read the Arabic sentence once to get the gist of the scholar's hadith studies.
Notice the locations mentioned: Baghdad and the Hijaz.
2
Identify the key elements
Identify that he heard hadith (samia al-hadith) with a group (ma'ahum) from the shaykhs of his time.
The phrase 'min mashayikh 'asrihi' indicates he learned from contemporary authorities.
3
Reflect on the significance
Consider why hearing hadith directly from shaykhs was important in his era. This was a traditional method of transmission.
Direct hearing (sama') was a key feature of hadith authentication.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فسمع معهم الحديث ببغداد والحجاز من مشايخ عصره، وكان في علم الفروسية واستعمال السلاح وما يتعلق به من أفراد العصر وله في ذلك الفن دقائق وعلوم أنفرد بها، وأما المجالس في التذكير والقعود فيما بين المريدين . وأسئلتهم عن الوقايع وخوضه فى الأجوبة وجريان الأحوال العجيبة فكلها منه واليه، أجمع أهل العصر على أنه عديم النظير فيها غير مشارك في أساليب الكلام على المسائل، وتطييب القلوب والاشارات اللطيفة المستنبطة من الآيات والأخبار من كلام المشايخ والرموز الدقيقة وتصانيفه فيها المشهورة، إلى غير ذلك من نظم الأشعار اللطيفة على لسان الطريقة ولقد عقد لنفسه مجلس الاملاء في الحديث سنة سبع وثلاثين وأربعمائة فكان يملى إلى خمس وستين يذنب أماليه بأبياته وربما يتكلم على الحديث باشاراته ولطائفه وله فى الكتابة طريقة أنيقة رشيقة تبن على النظم.
So he heard with them hadith in Baghdad and the Hijaz from the shaykhs of his time. He was in the science of horsemanship and the use of weapons and what pertains to that from among the unique individuals of the age, and in that art he had subtleties and sciences that he alone possessed. As for the gatherings for reminding and sitting among the disciples, and their questions about events, and his delving into answers, and the occurrence of wondrous states – all of it was from him and to him. The people of the age agreed that he was without peer in them, not sharing in the styles of speech on matters, and the delighting of hearts, and the subtle indications derived from verses and reports, from the speech of the shaykhs, and the precise symbols, and his famous works in them, besides that, the composition of subtle poems in the language of the path. And he held for himself a dictation session in hadith in the year 437 AH (1035 CE), and he continued dictating until [the year] 465? (maybe 465 AH?), adorning his dictations with his verses, and perhaps he would comment on the hadith with his indications and subtleties. And in writing he had an elegant and graceful style built upon poetry.
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage describes the scholar's multifaceted activities. During his Hajj journey, he heard hadith from shaykhs in Baghdad and the Hijaz. He was also an expert in horsemanship and weaponry, unique in his time. His teaching gatherings (majalis) for spiritual reminding were famous; he answered questions skillfully, and people agreed he had no equal in this. He composed subtle poems in the Sufi style. In 437 AH, he began an imla' (dictation) majlis for hadith, continuing until possibly 465 AH, embellishing his dictations with his own poetry and offering subtle commentary. His writing style was elegant and poetic.

Key Terms
الحديث
بغداد
الحجاز
مشايخ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which two regions did the scholar hear hadith?
A) Baghdad and the Hijaz
B) Damascus and Egypt
C) Kufa and Basra
D) Iraq and Persia

Key Takeaway
The scholar's hadith education involved direct hearing from shaykhs in two key Islamic centers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The scholar traveled to hear hadith from the shaykhs of his time. What sacrifices have you made to ensure your Islamic knowledge comes from qualified, living teachers?
?
You read that the scholar heard hadith in Baghdad and the Hijaz. Are you willing to leave your comfort zone to seek authentic knowledge, or do you settle for convenience?
?
The scholar listened directly to the shaykhs of his era. How many of your beliefs about Islam are based on direct, verified transmission from trustworthy scholars rather than hearsay or unverified sources?

Expertise in Horsemanship and Weaponry
Biographical mention of expertise in horsemanship and weaponry.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the scholar was also a unique expert in the science of horsemanship and weaponry.

Core Idea
He was a unique expert in the science of horsemanship and weaponry.

This passage highlights a lesser-known aspect of the scholar: his mastery of horsemanship and weaponry. He possessed subtleties and sciences that were unique to him in his time.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic sentence
Read the Arabic sentence focusing on the terms for horsemanship (furusiyya) and weapon use (isti'mal al-silah).
The phrase 'min afrad al-'asr' indicates he was among the unique individuals of the age.
2
Analyze the uniqueness
The text says he had 'daka'iq wa 'ulum' (subtleties and sciences) that he alone possessed. This suggests deep specialization.
Notice the phrase 'infarada biha' (he alone possessed them).
3
Consider the breadth of his knowledge
Reflect on how his expertise in martial arts complemented his religious scholarship, showing a well-rounded personality.
This demonstrates that Islamic scholars often excelled in multiple fields.

Teaching Gatherings and Spiritual Sessions
Description of the scholar's teaching gatherings and spiritual sessions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature of the scholar's teaching gatherings, including answering questions, spiritual states, and composition of poetry.

Core Idea
His teaching gatherings were unmatched in depth and style.

This passage describes the scholar's famous teaching sessions (majalis) for spiritual reminding. He answered disciples' questions, experienced wondrous states, and composed subtle poetry. His contemporaries agreed he was without peer in this art.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the passage about the gatherings (majalis) and note the key activities: reminding, sitting with disciples, answering questions, wondrous states.
The passage covers multiple aspects – it is a complex description.
2
Identify the consensus of contemporaries
The text says 'ajma'a ahl al-'asr' (the people of the age agreed) that he was without peer (adim al-nazir) in these gatherings.
This indicates high recognition of his unique teaching style.
3
Examine the components of his style
His style included 'asaleeb al-kalam' (styles of speech), delighting hearts, subtle indications from Quran and hadith, symbols, and his famous works.
He also composed subtle poems in the language of the path (tariqa).
4
Reflect on the poetry
Note that he composed 'nazm al-ash'ar al-latifa' (subtle poems) in the style of the Sufi path, indicating spiritual themes.
Poetry was used to convey deeper meanings.

He was also an expert in horsemanship and weaponry, unique in his time. His teaching gatherings (majalis) for spiritual reminding were famous; he answered questions skillfully, and people agreed he had no equal in this. He composed subtle poems in the Sufi style. In 437 AH, he began an imla' (dictation) majlis for hadith, continuing until possibly 465 AH, embellishing his dictations with his own poetry and offering subtle commentary. His writing style was elegant and poetic.

Key Terms
المجالس
التذكير
المريدين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The scholar's teaching sessions were purely academic lectures without spiritual depth.
Correction: They were spiritual sessions involving questions, states, and poetry, emphasizing both knowledge and heart.

Checkpoint

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
The passage mentions 'wondrous states' occurring in his sessions. Have you ever experienced a spiritual state that moved you beyond words? If not, are you willing to seek such gatherings, or are you satisfied with dry lectures?

Dictation Sessions and Elegant Writing
Description of the scholar's dictation sessions and writing style.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the scholar established a hadith dictation session and developed an elegant writing style based on poetry.

Core Idea
He established a hadith dictation session that showcased his poetic and scholarly abilities.

This passage tells us that in 437 AH the scholar started a dictation (imla') session for hadith, which he continued for many years. He embellished his dictations with his own poetry and commented on hadith with subtle indications. His writing style was elegant and based on poetic rhythm.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text about the dictation session (majlis al-imla').
Note the year: 437 AH, and the possible end year: 465 AH.
2
Identify the nature of the session
The session was for hadith dictation. He would dictate (yamli) hadith and adorn his dictations with his poetry.
The verb 'yudhannibu' (or 'yudhayyilu') means he adorned or appended his poetry.
3
Examine his commentary style
He would sometimes comment on hadith with his 'isharat' (indications) and 'lata'if' (subtleties).
This shows his unique interpretive approach.
4
Reflect on his writing style
His writing style was 'aniqa raqiqa' (elegant and graceful) and built upon poetry (tabanna 'ala al-nazm).
This indicates a poetic influence on his prose.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فسمع معهم الحديث ببغداد والحجاز من مشايخ عصره، وكان في علم الفروسية واستعمال السلاح وما يتعلق به من أفراد العصر وله في ذلك الفن دقائق وعلوم أنفرد بها، وأما المجالس في التذكير والقعود فيما بين المريدين . وأسئلتهم عن الوقايع وخوضه فى الأجوبة وجريان الأحوال العجيبة فكلها منه واليه، أجمع أهل العصر على أنه عديم النظير فيها غير مشارك في أساليب الكلام على المسائل، وتطييب القلوب والاشارات اللطيفة المستنبطة من الآيات والأخبار من كلام المشايخ والرموز الدقيقة وتصانيفه فيها المشهورة، إلى غير ذلك من نظم الأشعار اللطيفة على لسان الطريقة ولقد عقد لنفسه مجلس الاملاء في الحديث سنة سبع وثلاثين وأربعمائة فكان يملى إلى خمس وستين يذنب أماليه بأبياته وربما يتكلم على الحديث باشاراته ولطائفه وله فى الكتابة طريقة أنيقة رشيقة تبن على النظم.
So he heard with them hadith in Baghdad and the Hijaz from the shaykhs of his time. He was in the science of horsemanship and the use of weapons and what pertains to that from among the unique individuals of the age, and in that art he had subtleties and sciences that he alone possessed. As for the gatherings for reminding and sitting among the disciples, and their questions about events, and his delving into answers, and the occurrence of wondrous states – all of it was from him and to him. The people of the age agreed that he was without peer in them, not sharing in the styles of speech on matters, and the delighting of hearts, and the subtle indications derived from verses and reports, from the speech of the shaykhs, and the precise symbols, and his famous works in them, besides that, the composition of subtle poems in the language of the path. And he held for himself a dictation session in hadith in the year 437 AH (1035 CE), and he continued dictating until [the year] 465? (maybe 465 AH?), adorning his dictations with his verses, and perhaps he would comment on the hadith with his indications and subtleties. And in writing he had an elegant and graceful style built upon poetry.

He was also an expert in horsemanship and weaponry, unique in his time. ?

Praise from Dumyat al-Qasr
Quotation from Dumyat al-Qasr extolling the scholar's virtues.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a contemporary source praised the scholar's mastery of the Ash'ari school and his powerful preaching.

Core Idea
The scholar's virtues were so great that even Iblis would repent in his assembly.

This lesson presents a vivid contemporary testimony from Ali ibn al-Hasan's book 'Dumyat al-Qasr'. The author employs hyperbolic language to highlight the scholar's unique qualities, especially his command of Ash'ari theology and his rhetorical skill. As you read, note the literary style and the specific attributes praised.

Guided Path
1
Read the praise passage
Read the Arabic passage from 'Dumyat al-Qasr' once without analysis. Then read the translation to grasp the author's elevated tone.
The language is deliberately hyperbolic; notice phrases like 'if Iblis were tied...'
2
Identify the qualities praised
List the attributes attributed to the scholar: being a collector of virtues, skilled in Ash'ari speaking, vast knowledge, poetic talent, etc.
The author emphasizes both intellectual and spiritual impact.
3
Reflect on the purpose of such praise
Consider why biographers include such laudatory quotes. They establish the scholar's reputation and influence among contemporaries.
This quote is not just flattery but a witness to his authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولقد قرات فصلا ذكره على بن الحسن فى دمية القصر وهو أن قال الإمام زين الإسلام أبو القسم جامع لانواع المحاسن تنقاد له صعابها ذلل المراسن ولو قرع الصخر بسوط تحذيره لذاب ولو ربط إبليس فى مجلس تذكيره لتاب، وله فصل الخطاب فى فضل المنطق المستطاب ماهر فى التكلم على مذهب الأشعرى، خارج في إحاطته بالعلوم عن الحد البشرى كلماته للمستفيدين فزائد وفوائد، وعتبات منبره للعارفين وسائدوله شعر يتتوج به رؤوس معاليه إذا ختمت به أذناب أماليه قال عبد الغافر وقد أخذ طريق التصوف من الاستاذ أبي علي الدقاق وأخذها أبو على عن أبي القسم النصر اباذي والنصراباذى عن الشبلي والشبلى عن الجنيد والجنيد عن السري السقطي والسرى عن معروف الكرخى ومعروف عن داود الطائي وداود لقى التابعين هكذا كان يذكر إسناد طريقته.
And I have read a chapter mentioned by Ali ibn al-Hasan in Dumyat al-Qasr, in which he said: 'The Imam, the Ornament of Islam, Abu al-Qasim, is a collector of all kinds of virtues; their difficulties submit to him, their obstacles are easy. If one were to strike a rock with the whip of his warning, it would melt; and if Iblis were tied in his reminding assembly, he would repent. He has the decisive speech concerning the excellence of the beloved logic; he is skilled in speaking upon the Ash'ari school; in his encompassing of sciences he exceeds the human limit. His words for students are increasing advantages, and the thresholds of his pulpit for the knowers are cushions. He has poetry that adorns the heights of his high stations when the ends of his dictations are concluded with it.' 'Abd al-Ghafir said: 'He took the path of tasawwuf from the master Abu Ali al-Daqqaq; Abu Ali took it from Abu al-Qasim al-Nasrabadhi; al-Nasrabadhi from al-Shibli; al-Shibli from al-Junayd; al-Junayd from al-Sari al-Saqati; al-Sari from Ma'ruf al-Karkhi; Ma'ruf from Dawud al-Ta'i; and Dawud met the Tabi'un.' Thus he used to mention the chain of his path.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage contains two parts. First, a quotation from Ali ibn al-Hasan's book 'Dumyat al-Qasr', which extols the scholar in highly elevated language, emphasizing his mastery of the Ash'ari school, his vast knowledge, and the power of his preaching. The quote also notes his poetry. Second, 'Abd al-Ghafir records the scholar's Sufi chain (silsila), showing his spiritual lineage through a series of famous early Sufis back to Dawud al-Ta'i, who met the Tabi'un (the generation after the Prophet's Companions). This validates his authority in tasawwuf.

Key Terms
دمية القصر
فصل الخطاب
المذهب الأشعري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which school of theology is the scholar said to be skilled in speaking upon?
A) Hanafi
B) Ash'ari
C) Maturidi
D) Zahiri

Key Takeaway
The scholar was praised for his mastery of Ash'ari theology, powerful preaching, vast knowledge, and poetic skill.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your life were described in such hyperbolic praise as this scholar's, what single virtue would others highlight? Are you actively cultivating that virtue, or are you coasting on good intentions?
?
The scholar's words are called 'increasing advantages' (فوائد). Whom are you benefiting with your knowledge and presence? Think of one person you will intentionally benefit today—not just with information, but with real spiritual or practical help.
?
You just read that even Iblis would repent in his assembly. Is there a sin or habit in your life that you continue to defend, despite knowing it displeases Allah? What concrete step will you take today to truly repent—not just feel sorry, but change?

The Sufi Spiritual Lineage
Records the scholar's Sufi chain back to the Tabi'un.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the significance of the Sufi chain (silsila) that connects the scholar to the early generations of Muslims.

Core Idea
The scholar's spiritual authority is validated through an unbroken chain of Sufi masters back to the Tabi'un.

This lesson records the scholar's Sufi lineage as noted by 'Abd al-Ghafir. Chains of transmission (sanad) are crucial in Islamic scholarship, and this one traces back to Dawud al-Ta'i, who met the Tabi'un. Pay attention to the named figures and the value placed on such chains.

Guided Path
1
Read the chain passage
Read the Arabic passage listing the Sufi chain. Then read the translation to follow the names in order.
The chain is presented as a sequence of 'took from' statements.
2
Identify each link in the chain
List each master in order from the scholar back to Dawud al-Ta'i. Note how many generations are involved.
There are eight named individuals before the Tabi'un are mentioned.
3
Understand the function of the chain
Reflect on why the biographer included this lineage. It authenticates the scholar's spiritual path (tariqa) and connects him to the early Sufi tradition.
The chain ends with Dawud al-Ta'i, who met the Tabi'un, giving it a direct link to the first generations.

Persecution and Exile of a Scholar
Narrates the scholar's persecution due to sectarian conflict and his journey to Baghdad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical circumstances of a scholar's trial due to sectarian fanaticism and his response in seeking refuge with the caliph.

Core Idea
Sectarian envy drove a scholar from his home, but the caliph's acceptance restored honor.

This passage recounts a painful episode in Islamic scholarship: a respected scholar was targeted by sectarian bigots and slandered until his teaching circles were shut down. Forced to leave his homeland, he journeyed to Baghdad and sought the protection of the Abbasid Caliph, who received him with honor. This story illustrates both the dangers of factionalism and the value of just leadership.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text and its translation. Notice the key terms like 'trial' (محنة) and 'fanaticism' (تعصب). The passage is a single narrative paragraph.
Pay attention to the dates: 440-455 AH.
2
Identify the causes of persecution
The text mentions 'fanaticism between the two groups', 'inclination of governors to whims', and 'slandering by leaders and judges'. These are the causes.
Envy (حسد) is also cited as a motive.
3
Trace the consequences
The persecution led to 'cessation of gatherings', 'dispersal of companions', and the scholar's forced departure from his homeland. He then traveled to Baghdad.
4
Reflect on the resolution
The Caliph al-Qa'im bi-Amr Allah accepted him and held a gathering in his residence. This shows a positive outcome despite hardship.
The scholar found safety and honor in Baghdad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن جملة أحواله ما خص به من المحنة في الدين والاعتقاد وظهو التعصب بين الفريقين فى عشر سنه أربعين إلى خمس وخمسين وأربعمائة وميل بعض الولاة إلى الاهواء وسعى بعض الرؤساء والقضاة إليه بالتخليط حتى أدى ذلك إلى رفع المجالس وتفرق شمل الأصحاب وكان هو المقصود من بينهم حسداً حتى اضطرته الحال إلى مفارقة الأوطان وامتد في أثناء ذلك إلى بغداد وورد على أمير المؤمنين القائم بأمر الله، ولقى فيها قبولا وعقد له المجلس في منازله المختصة به وكان.
And among his circumstances was that which was particularly his of the trial in religion and belief, and the appearance of fanaticism between the two groups in the decade of [the years] 440 to 455 AH, and the inclination of some governors to whims, and the slandering of some leaders and judges against him with allegations of confusion, until that led to the cessation of gatherings and the dispersal of the companions. He was the intended target among them out of envy, so necessity forced him to leave his homeland. He extended during that to Baghdad and arrived before the Commander of the Faithful, al-Qa'im bi-Amr Allah. He met with acceptance there, and a gathering was held for him in his private residence.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage describes the scholar's persecution. Between the years 440 and 455 AH (c. 1048-1063 CE), sectarian fanaticism (likely between Ash'aris and Hanbalis or other groups) intensified. Some governors and judges were biased and slandered him, leading to the disruption of his teaching circles and the dispersal of his followers. He was singled out due to envy. As a result, he was forced to leave his home region. He traveled to Baghdad and sought the audience of the Abbasid Caliph al-Qa'im bi-Amr Allah, who received him honorably and allowed him to hold gatherings in his residence.

Key Terms
المحنة
التعصب
القائم بأمر الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The scholar's trial was due to his own wrongdoing or heretical views.
Correction: The text clearly states that he was targeted out of envy (حسد) and slandered by biased individuals, not because of any fault in his belief or conduct.

Checkpoint
Why was the scholar forced to leave his homeland?
A) He was accused of heresy
B) Sectarian fanaticism and slander
C) He wanted to perform Hajj
D) He was appointed as a judge elsewhere

Key Takeaway
Persecution can arise from envy and sectarianism, but seeking refuge with just authority can lead to honor and safety.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever been falsely accused or mistreated because of someone's envy or sectarian bias? How did you respond, and can you see yourself turning to a just authority as the scholar did instead of seeking revenge?
?
When you witness division among Muslims today, do you recognize the role of personal whims and envy as this passage highlights? What specific step can you take to avoid being a source of such division?
?
Would you be willing to leave your home and comfort if necessity forced you for the sake of your beliefs? Are you prepared to trust that Allah will provide refuge and honor as He did for this scholar through a just ruler?

Al-Qushayri's Scholarly Excellence and Unique Talents
Description of al-Qushayri's comprehensive knowledge and dictation sessions with a laudatory quote

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the breadth of Abu al-Qasim al-Qushayri's knowledge and his unique abilities in hadith, horsemanship, dictation, and poetry.

Core Idea
Al-Qushayri was a master of both exoteric sciences and spiritual allusions.

This passage from Ibn 'Asakir's Tabyin Kadhib al-Muftari presents a vivid portrait of Imam al-Qushayri's multifaceted genius. From his mastery of hadith and horsemanship to his elegant poetry and dictation sessions, we see a scholar who combined outward learning with inward depth.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing to analyze. Then read the translation to get a sense of the narrative flow.
Notice the shift from describing his scholarly attainments to the praise from Damyat al-Qasr.
2
Identify the areas of expertise

4

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحديث ببغداد والحجاز من مشايخ عصره، وكان في علم الفروسية واستعمال السلاح وما يتعلق به من أفراد العصر وله في ذلك الفن دقائق وعلوم أنفرد بها، وأما المجالس في التذكير والقعود فيما بين المريدين. وأسئلتهم عن الوقايع وخوضه في الأجوبة وجريان الأحوال العجيبة فكلها منه واليه، أجمع أهل العصر على أنه عديم النظير فيها غير مشارك في أساليب الكلام على المسائل، وتطيب القلوب والاشارات اللطيفة المستنبطة من الآيات والأخبار من كلام المشايخ والرموز الدقيقة وتصانيفه فيها المشهورة، إلى غير ذلك من نظم الأشعار اللطيفة على لسان الطريقة ولقد عقد لنفسه مجلس الاملاء في الحديث سنة سبع وثلاثين وأربعمائة فكان يملي إلى خمس وستين يذنب أماليه بأبياته وربما يتكلم على الحديث باشاراته ولطائفه وله في الكتابة طريقة أنيقة رشيقة تبنى على النظم، ولقد قرأت فصلا ذكره علي بن الحسن في (دمية القصر) وهو أن قال الإمام زين الإسلام أبو القاسم جامع لانواع المحاسن تنقاد له صعابها ذلل المراسن ولو قرع الصخر بسوط تحذيره لذاب ولو ربط إبليس في مجلس تذكيره لتاب، وله فصل الخطاب في فضل المنطق المستطاب ماهر في التكلم على مذهب الأشعري، خارج في إحاطته بالعلوم عن الحد البشري كلماته للمستفيدين فرائد وفوائد، وعتبات منبره للعارفين وسائد. وله شعر يتوجه به رؤوس معاليه إذا ختمت به أذناب أماليه، قال عبد الغافر وقد أخذ طريق التصوف من الاستاذ أبي علي الدقاق وأخذها أبو علي عن أبي القاسم النصراباذي والنصراباذي عن الشبلي والشبلي عن الجنيد والجنيد عن السري السقطي والسري عن معروف الكرخي ومعروف عن داود الطائي وداود لقي التابعين هكذا كان يذكر إسناد طريقته، ومن جملة أحواله ما خص به من المحنة في الدين والاعتقاد وظهور التعصب بين الفريقين في عشر سنه أربعين إلى خمس وخمسين وأربعمائة وميل بعض الولاة إلى الاهواء وسعي بعض الرؤساء والقضاة إليه بالتخليط حتى أدى ذلك إلى رفع المجالس وتفرق شمل الأصحاب وكان هو المقصود من بينهم حسدا حتى اضطرته الحال إلى مفارقة الأوطان وامتد في أثناء ذلك إلى بغداد وورد على أمير المؤمنين القائم بأمر الله، ولقي فيها قبولا وعقد له المجلس في منازله المختصة به وكان ذلك بمحضر ومرأى منه، ووقع كلامه من مجلسه الموقع وخرج الأمر باعزازه وإكرامه وعاد إلى نيسابور وكان يختلف منها إلى طوس بأهله وبعض أولاده، حتى طلع صبح النوبة المباركة دولة السلطان البارسلان سنة خمس وخمسين وأربعمائة، فبقي عشر سنين في آخر عمره مرفوعا محترما مطاعا معظما وأكثر صفوه في آخر أيامه التي شاهدناه فيها أخيرا إلى أن يقرأ عليه كتبه والأحاديث المسموعة له، وما يؤول إلى نصرة المذهب بلغ المنتمون إليه آلافا ملؤا بذكره وتصانيفه أطرافا، ومن نثره الكرم أطال الله بقاء الشيخ يهدي المتوسم إلى صاحبه ويقضي للمؤمل بنجح مطالبه، وأنى أجلت صواعد قصدي في كل قطر أشيم برق الحرية وأعملت قواصد فكري في كل نحو أستنشق نسيم الفتوة فما فاح إلا من بابه نشره وما لاح إلا من جنابه بشره فتعرفت إليه بأني ممن هداه إلى وده بقاء عهده وحداه على قصده ضيا مجده وأرجوانه، إذا عجم عود ولائي استصلبه وإذا قيد قلبي بإحسانه ما سيبه، والله عز وجل يديم تمكينه ويحرس عن الغير نعمته ودينه بمنه أن وجد الشيخ في مجلس العميد فراغا وللمنطق مساغا طالعه بأن فلانا إلى الباب متردد، وباقامة رسم الزيارة مستسعد وليس يشكو تحمله خجلة الحجاب ولكنه يشكو تجمله بحضور الباب والسلام، توفي صبيحة يوم الأحد قبل طلوع الشمس السادس عشر من شهر ربيع الآخر سنة خمس وستين وأربعمائة ودفن في المدرسة بجنب الأستاذ أبي علي الدقاق
Hadith in Baghdad and the Hijaz from the scholars of his era. He was in the science of horsemanship and the use of weapons and what pertains to it among the unique individuals of the age, and for him in that art there are subtleties and sciences he alone possessed. As for the assemblies of reminding and sitting among the disciples, and their questions about events, and his sinking into answers, and the flow of wondrous states, all of it proceeds from him and returns to him. The people of the era agreed that he was without equal in this, not sharing in the styles of speech on issues, and pleasing hearts, and the delicate allusions derived from the verses and reports from the speech of the shaykhs, and the precise symbols, and his famous writings in that. And besides that, the composition of delicate poems in the language of the Path. And indeed he held a dictation session in hadith in the year 437 AH, and he would dictate until [age] 65, making his dictations with his poems, and perhaps he would speak on the hadith with his allusions and subtleties. And in writing he had an elegant, graceful style built on verse. And I read a chapter mentioned by Ali ibn al-Hasan in (Damyat al-Qasr) that he said: The Imam Zayn al-Islam Abu al-Qasim is a collector of all types of beauties; their difficulties submit to him, docile in reins. If he were to strike a rock with the whip of his warning, it would melt. If he were to bind Iblis in his assembly of reminding, he would repent. He has decisive speech on the virtue of excellent logic, an expert in speaking on the Ash'ari school, beyond the human limit in his encompassing of sciences. His words are benefits and advantages for those who seek benefit, and the thresholds of his pulpit are pillows for the knowers. He has poetry that crowns the heads of his highnesses when the tails of his dictations are concluded with it. Abd al-Ghafir said: He took the path of tasawwuf from the master Abu Ali al-Daqqaq, and Abu Ali took it from Abu al-Qasim al-Nasrabadhi, and al-Nasrabadhi from al-Shibli, and al-Shibli from al-Junayd, and al-Junayd from al-Sari al-Saqati, and al-Sari from Ma'ruf al-Karkhi, and Ma'ruf from Dawud al-Ta'i, and Dawud met the Successors. Thus he would mention the chain of his path. And among his circumstances was what was specially decreed for him of tribulation in religion and belief, and the appearance of partisanship between the two groups in the decade of the years 440 to 455 AH, and the inclination of some governors to passions, and the striving of some chiefs and judges against him with confusion, until that led to the raising of assemblies and the dispersal of the companions, and he was the target among them out of envy, until circumstances forced him to leave his homelands. And during that he extended to Baghdad and came before the Commander of the Faithful al-Qa'im bi-Amr Allah, and he received acceptance there, and assemblies were held for him in his private residences, and that was in his presence and sight. And his speech from his assembly had effect, and the command went out to honor and respect him, and he returned to Nishapur, and he would travel from there to Tus with his family and some of his children, until the morning of the blessed turn appeared, the state of Sultan Alp Arslan in the year 455 AH. So he remained ten years at the end of his life, elevated, respected, obeyed, glorified, and most of his leisure in his last days in which we saw him finally was for reading his books and the hadith he had heard, and what would lead to the support of the school. Those affiliated with it reached thousands, filling regions with his mention and his writings. And from his generous prose: 'May God prolong the life of the shaykh. He guides the spectator to his companion and fulfills for the hopeful the success of his goals. I have directed the peaks of my intention in every region to see the lightning of freedom, and I have employed the intentions of my thought in every direction to inhale the breeze of chivalry. It wafted only from his door, and shone only from his countenance. So I recognized him by that I am among those whom the endurance of his covenant guided to his love, and the light of his glory urged towards his intent. If the wood of my loyalty is tested, he finds it solid; if my heart is fettered by his generosity, nothing releases it. May God Almighty perpetuate his authority and guard his blessing and his religion from others, by His grace. When the shaykh found in the assembly of the 'amid a respite and for logic a passage, he perused that so-and-so is frequenting the door, and is blessed by maintaining the rite of visitation. He does not complain of the burden of the embarrassment of the veil, but complains of his adornment by attending the door and the greeting.' He died on the morning of Sunday, before sunrise, the 16th of Rabi' al-Akhir, 465 AH, and was buried in the school next to the master Abu Ali al-Daqqaq.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage is a continuous biographical account of Imam Abu al-Qasim al-Qushayri (Zayn al-Islam), a leading Ash'ari theologian and Sufi master. It follows the author's sequence: first, it describes his comprehensive knowledge—including hadith, horsemanship, and the art of weapons—and his unique ability to address disciples' questions with subtle allusions and poetry. Next, it highlights his dictation sessions and his elegant writing style, then quotes a praise from Ali ibn al-Hasan's 'Damyat al-Qasr' extolling his rhetorical power and his mastery of the Ash'ari school. The biography then traces his Sufi lineage through a golden chain back to the Successors, emphasizing his spiritual authority. It proceeds to narrate the fitna (persecution) he faced around 440-455 AH due to sectarian partisanship, which forced him to flee to Baghdad, where he was honored by the caliph. After returning to Nishapur, he later enjoyed a decade of honor under Sultan Alp Arslan until his death in 465 AH. The passage concludes with a sample of his elegant prose and details of his death and burial beside Abu Ali al-Daqqaq. The commentary follows the author's narrative order, explaining each element—from his scholarly attainments, to his spiritual lineage, to his trials and final years—as a unified portrait of a multifaceted saint-scholar.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think al-Qushayri was solely a Sufi mystic with little formal learning.
Correction: This passage shows he was also a master of hadith, horsemanship, weapons, and the Ash'ari school, demonstrating a synthesis of outward and inward sciences.

Checkpoint
In which year did Abu al-Qasim al-Qushayri hold his first dictation (imla') session?
A) 400 AH
B) 437 AH
C) 455 AH
D) 465 AH

Key Takeaway
Al-Qushayri was a polymath who combined exoteric knowledge, spiritual subtlety, and poetic elegance in a way that his contemporaries considered unparalleled.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Qushayri combined deep formal learning with spiritual subtlety. In your own life, do you prioritize one over the other? What would it take for you to seek both with the same intensity starting today?
?
The passage says his words were 'benefits and advantages for those who seek benefit.' Are you truly seeking benefit from what you learn, or are you just accumulating information? What specific change will you make today to become a seeker of benefit?
?
He held dictation sessions until age 65. What is your commitment to lifelong learning? Are you making excuses for your own stagnation, or are you actively pursuing growth in knowledge and character? What one step will you take this week to emulate his dedication?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner
4 min
Al-Qushayri's Sufi Lineage and Spiritual Chain
Chain of transmission for al-Qushayri's Sufi path, from his teacher back to the Successors

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the spiritual lineage of Imam al-Qushayri and the importance of this chain in establishing his authority as a Sufi master.

Core Idea
Al-Qushayri's Sufi chain links him to the great early mystics, authenticating his spiritual transmission.

This brief but significant passage traces the lineage of Imam al-Qushayri's Sufi path. By naming the chain of masters from his own teacher back to the Successors, it grounds his spiritual authority in an unbroken line of transmission.

Guided Path
1
Read the chain carefully
Read the Arabic passage and translation, noting each name in the chain. Observe how each shaykh transmitted the path to the next.
The chain is an isnad for tasawwuf, similar to hadith transmission.
2
Recognize the significance of the chain
Understand that this chain connects al-Qushayri to al-Junayd and then to the Successors, giving his Sufi practice a prophetic root.
Al-Junayd is a central figure; Dawud al-Ta'i met the tabi'un.
3
Reflect on the phrase 'طريق التصوف'
Consider what 'path of tasawwuf' meant in the 5th century AH. This chain shows it was a transmitted discipline.
4
Memorize or write the chain
Try to reproduce the chain from memory. This helps internalize the spiritual lineage.

الحديث ببغداد والحجاز من مشايخ عصره، وكان في علم الفروسية واستعمال السلاح وما يتعلق به من أفراد العصر وله في ذلك الفن دقائق وعلوم أنفرد بها، وأما المجالس في التذكير والقعود فيما بين المريدين. وأسئلتهم Hadith in Baghdad and the Hijaz from the scholars of his era. He was in the science of horsemanship and the use of weapons and what pertains to it among the unique individuals of the age, and for him in that art there are subtleties and sciences he alone possessed. As for the assemblies of reminding and sitting among the disciples, and their questions about events, and his sinking into answers, and the flow of wondrous states, all of it proceeds from him and returns to him. The people of the era agreed that he was without equal in this, not sharing in the styles of speech on issues, and pleasing hearts, and the delicate allusions derived from the verses and reports from the speech of the shaykhs, and the precise symbols, and his famous writings in that. And besides that, the composition of delicate poems in the language of the Path. And indeed he held a dictation session in hadith in the year 437 AH, and he would dictate until [age] 65, making his dictations with his poems, and perhaps he would speak on the hadith with his allusions and subtleties. And in writing he had an elegant, graceful style built on verse. And I read a chapter mentioned by Ali ibn al-Hasan in (Damyat al-Qasr) that he said: The Imam Zayn al-Islam Abu al-Qasim is a collector of all types of beauties; their difficulties submit to him, docile in reins. If he were to strike a rock with the whip of his warning, it would melt. If he were to bind Iblis in his assembly of reminding, he would repent. His words are benefits and advantages for those who seek benefit, and the thresholds of his pulpit are pillows for the knowers. Abd al-Ghafir said: He took the path of tasawwuf from the master Abu Ali al-Daqqaq, and Abu Ali took it from Abu al-Qasim al-Nasrabadhi, and al-Nasrabadhi from al-Shibli, and al-Shibli from al-Junayd, and al-Junayd from al-Sari al-Saqati, and al-Sari from Ma'ruf al-Karkhi, and Ma'ruf from Dawud al-Ta'i, and Dawud met the Successors. Thus he would mention the chain of his path. And among his circumstances was what was specially decreed for him of tribulation in religion and belief, and the appearance of partisanship between the two groups in the decade of the years 440 to 455 AH, and the inclination of some governors to passions, and the striving of some chiefs and judges against him with confusion, until that led to the raising of assemblies and the dispersal of the companions, and he was the target among them out of envy, until circumstances forced him to leave his homelands. And during that he extended to Baghdad and came before the Commander of the Faithful al-Qa'im bi-Amr Allah, and he received acceptance there, and assemblies were held for him in his private residences, and that was in his presence and sight. And his speech from his assembly had effect, and the command went out to honor and respect him, and he returned to Nishapur, and he would travel from there to Tus with his family and some of his children, until the morning of the blessed turn appeared, the state of Sultan Alp Arslan in the year 455 AH. Those affiliated with it reached thousands, filling regions with his mention and his writings. And from his generous prose: 'May God prolong the life of the shaykh. He guides the spectator to his companion and fulfills for the hopeful the success of his goals. I have directed the peaks of my intention in every region to see the lightning of freedom, and I have employed the intentions of my thought in every direction to inhale the breeze of chivalry. It wafted only from his door, and shone only from his countenance. So I recognized him by that I am among those whom the endurance of his covenant guided to his love, and the light of his glory urged towards his intent. If the wood of my loyalty is tested, he finds it solid; if my heart is fettered by his generosity, nothing releases it. May God Almighty perpetuate his authority and guard his blessing and his religion from others, by His grace. When the shaykh found in the assembly of the 'amid a respite and for logic a passage, he perused that so-and-so is frequenting the door, and is blessed by maintaining the rite of visitation. He does not complain of the burden of the embarrassment of the veil, but complains of his adornment by attending the door and the greeting.' He died on the morning of Sunday, before sunrise, the 16th of Rabi' al-Akhir, 465 AH, and was buried in the school next to the master Abu Ali al-Daqqaq.

Commentary
This passage is a continuous biographical account of Imam Abu al-Qasim al-Qushayri (Zayn al-Islam), a leading Ash'ari theologian and Sufi master. It follows the author's sequence: first, it describes his comprehensive knowledge—including hadith, horsemanship, and the art of weapons—and his unique ability to address disciples' questions with subtle allusions and poetry. Next, it highlights his dictation sessions and his elegant writing style, then quotes a praise from Ali ibn al-Hasan's 'Damyat al-Qasr' extolling his rhetorical power and his mastery of the Ash'ari school. The biography then traces his Sufi lineage through a golden chain back to the Successors, emphasizing his spiritual authority. It proceeds to narrate the fitna (persecution) he faced around 440-455 AH due to sectarian partisanship, which forced him to flee to Baghdad, where he was honored by the caliph. After returning to Nishapur, he later enjoyed a decade of honor under Sultan Alp Arslan until his death in 465 AH. The passage concludes with a sample of his elegant prose and details of his death and burial beside Abu Ali al-Daqqaq. The commentary follows the author's narrative order, explaining each element—from his scholarly attainments, to his spiritual lineage, to his trials and final years—as a unified portrait of a multifaceted saint-scholar.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
The chain ends with Dawud al-Ta'i meeting the Successors—those who knew the Companions. Do you feel any personal responsibility to preserve and pass on authentic Islamic knowledge to the next generation? How will you ensure the chain does not break with you?

Persecution and Final Years of al-Qushayri
Narrative of al-Qushayri's persecution, exile, return to honor, and death, with a sample of his prose

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the trials faced by al-Qushayri due to sectarian conflict, his exile to Baghdad, his return to honor, and his death.

Core Idea
Al-Qushayri endured persecution for his beliefs but ultimately found honor and left a lasting legacy.

This concluding section of the biography narrates the fitna that befell al-Qushayri, his flight to Baghdad, his rehabilitation under Sultan Alp Arslan, and his final years. It also includes a sample of his elegant prose and details of his death.

Guided Path
1
Read about the persecution
Read the passage focusing on the fitna – what caused it, who was involved, and how al-Qushayri was singled out. Note the time frame (440-455 AH).
The persecution was due to sectarian partisanship and envy.
2
Follow his journey to Baghdad
Trace al-Qushayri's exile: he went to Baghdad, met the caliph al-Qa'im, and received honor. How did the caliph receive him?
He was allowed to hold assemblies and was honored.
3
Note his return and later years
After returning to Nishapur, he enjoyed ten years of honor under Sultan Alp Arslan. What does the passage say about his activities?
He continued teaching and supporting the Ash'ari school.
4
Read the prose sample and death account
The passage includes a sample of his prose. Read it as an example of his style. Then note the exact date and place of his death and burial.
He died on Sunday, 16 Rabi' al-Akhir 465 AH, and was buried next to his teacher Abu Ali al-Daqqaq.

الحديث ببغداد والحجاز من مشايخ عصره، وكان في علم الفروسية واستعمال السلاح وما يتعلق به من أفراد العصر وله في ذلك الفن دقائق وعلوم أنفرد بها، وأما المجالس في التذكير والقعود فيما بين المريدين. وأسئلتهم عن الوقايع وخوضه في الأجوبة وجريان الأحوال العجيبة فكلها منه واليه، أجمع أهل العصر على أنه عديم النظير فيها غير مشارك في أساليب الكلام على المسائل، وتطيب القلوب والاشارات اللطيفة المستنبطة من الآيات والأخبار من كلام المشايخ والرموز الدقيقة وتصانيفه فيها المشهورة، إلى غير ذلك من نظم الأشعار اللطيفة على لسان الطريقة ولقد عقد لنفسه مجلس الاملاء في الحديث سنة سبع وثلاثين وأربعمائة فكان يملي إلى خمس وستين يذنب أماليه بأبياته وربما يتكلم على الحديث باشاراته ولطائفه وله في الكتابة طريقة أنيقة رشيقة تبنى على النظم، ولقد قرأت فصلا ذكره علي بن الحسن في (دمية القصر) وهو أن قال الإمام زين الإسلام أبو القاسم جامع لانواع المحاسن تنقاد له صعابها ذلل المراسن ولو قرع الصخر بسوط تحذيره لذاب ولو ربط إبليس في مجلس تذكيره لتاب، وله فصل الخطاب في فضل المنطق المستطاب ماهر في التكلم على مذهب الأشعري، خارج في إحاطته بالعلوم عن الحد البشري كلماته للمستفيدين فرائد وفوائد، وعتبات منبره للعارفين وسائد. وله شعر يتوجه به رؤوس معاليه إذا ختمت به أذناب أماليه، قال عبد الغافر وقد أخذ طريق التصوف من الاستاذ أبي علي الدقاق وأخذها أبو علي عن أبي القاسم النصراباذي والنصراباذي عن الشبلي والشبلي عن الجنيد والجنيد عن السري السقطي والسري عن معروف الكرخي ومعروف عن داود الطائي وداود لقي التابعين هكذا كان يذكر إسناد طريقته، ومن جملة أحواله ما خص به من المحنة في الدين والاعتقاد وظهور التعصب بين الفريقين في عشر سنه أربعين إلى خمس وخمسين وأربعمائة وميل بعض الولاة إلى الاهواء وسعي بعض الرؤساء والقضاة إليه بالتخليط حتى أدى ذلك إلى رفع المجالس وتفرق شمل الأصحاب وكان هو المقصود من بينهم حسدا حتى اضطرته الحال إلى مفارقة الأوطان وامتد في أثناء ذلك إلى بغداد وورد على أمير المؤمنين القائم بأمر الله، ولقي فيها قبولا وعقد له المجلس في منازله المختصة به وكان ذلك بمحضر ومرأى منه، ووقع كلامه من مجلسه الموقع وخرج الأمر باعزازه وإكرامه وعاد إلى نيسابور وكان يختلف منها إلى طوس بأهله وبعض أولاده، حتى طلع صبح النوبة المباركة دولة السلطان البارسلان سنة خمس وخمسين وأربعمائة، فبقي عشر سنين في آخر عمره مرفوعا محترما مطاعا معظما وأكثر صفوه في آخر أيامه التي شاهدناه فيها أخيرا إلى أن يقرأ عليه كتبه والأحاديث المسموعة له، وما يؤول إلى نصرة المذهب بلغ المنتمون إليه آلافا ملؤا بذكره وتصانيفه أطرافا، ومن نثره الكرم أطال الله بقاء الشيخ يهدي المتوسم إلى صاحبه ويقضي للمؤمل بنجح مطالبه، وأنى أجلت صواعد قصدي في كل قطر أشيم برق الحرية وأعملت قواصد فكري في كل نحو أستنشق نسيم الفتوة فما فاح إلا من بابه نشره وما لاح إلا من جنابه بشره فتعرفت إليه بأني ممن هداه إلى وده بقاء عهده وحداه على قصده ضيا مجده وأرجوانه، إذا عجم عود ولائي استصلبه وإذا قيد قلبي بإحسانه ما سيبه، والله عز وجل يديم تمكينه ويحرس عن الغير نعمته ودينه بمنه أن وجد الشيخ في مجلس العميد فراغا وللمنطق مساغا طالعه بأن فلانا إلى الباب متردد، وباقامة رسم الزيارة مستسعد وليس يشكو تحمله خجلة الحجاب ولكنه يشكو تجمله بحضور الباب والسلام، توفي صبيحة يوم الأحد قبل طلوع الشمس السادس عشر من شهر ربيع الآخر سنة خمس وستين وأربعمائة ودفن في المدرسة بجنب الأستاذ أبي علي الدقاق
Hadith in Baghdad and the Hijaz from the scholars of his era. He was in the science of horsemanship and the use of weapons and what pertains to it among the unique individuals of the age, and for him in that art there are subtleties and sciences he alone possessed. As for the assemblies of reminding and sitting among the disciples, and their questions about events, and his sinking into answers, and the flow of wondrous states, all of it proceeds from him and returns to him. The people of the era agreed that he was without equal in this, not sharing in the styles of speech on issues, and pleasing hearts, and the delicate allusions derived from the verses and reports from the speech of the shaykhs, and the precise symbols, and his famous writings in that. And besides that, the composition of delicate poems in the language of the Path. And indeed he held a dictation session in hadith in the year 437 AH, and he would dictate until [age] 65, making his dictations with his poems, and perhaps he would speak on the hadith with his allusions and subtleties. And in writing he had an elegant, graceful style built on verse. And I read a chapter mentioned by Ali ibn al-Hasan in (Damyat al-Qasr) that he said: The Imam Zayn al-Islam Abu al-Qasim is a collector of all types of beauties; their difficulties submit to him, docile in reins. If he were to strike a rock with the whip of his warning, it would melt. If he were to bind Iblis in his assembly of reminding, he would repent. He has decisive speech on the virtue of excellent logic, an expert in speaking on the Ash'ari school, beyond the human limit in his encompassing of sciences. His words are benefits and advantages for those who seek benefit, and the thresholds of his pulpit are pillows for the knowers. He has poetry that crowns the heads of his highnesses when the tails of his dictations are concluded with it. Abd al-Ghafir said: He took the path of tasawwuf from the master Abu Ali al-Daqqaq, and Abu Ali took it from Abu al-Qasim al-Nasrabadhi, and al-Nasrabadhi from al-Shibli, and al-Shibli from al-Junayd, and al-Junayd from al-Sari al-Saqati, and al-Sari from Ma'ruf al-Karkhi, and Ma'ruf from Dawud al-Ta'i, and Dawud met the Successors. Thus he would mention the chain of his path. And among his circumstances was what was specially decreed for him of tribulation in religion and belief, and the appearance of partisanship between the two groups in the decade of the years 440 to 455 AH, and the inclination of some governors to passions, and the striving of some chiefs and judges against him with confusion, until that led to the raising of assemblies and the dispersal of the companions, and he was the target among them out of envy, until circumstances forced him to leave his homelands. And during that he extended to Baghdad and came before the Commander of the Faithful al-Qa'im bi-Amr Allah, and he received acceptance there, and assemblies were held for him in his private residences, and that was in his presence and sight. And his speech from his assembly had effect, and the command went out to honor and respect him, and he returned to Nishapur, and he would travel from there to Tus with his family and some of his children, until the morning of the blessed turn appeared, the state of Sultan Alp Arslan in the year 455 AH. So he remained ten years at the end of his life, elevated, respected, obeyed, glorified, and most of his leisure in his last days in which we saw him finally was for reading his books and the hadith he had heard, and what would lead to the support of the school. Those affiliated with it reached thousands, filling regions with his mention and his writings. And from his generous prose: 'May God prolong the life of the shaykh. He guides the spectator to his companion and fulfills for the hopeful the success of his goals. I have directed the peaks of my intention in every region to see the lightning of freedom, and I have employed the intentions of my thought in every direction to inhale the breeze of chivalry. It wafted only from his door, and shone only from his countenance. So I recognized him by that I am among those whom the endurance of his covenant guided to his love, and the light of his glory urged towards his intent. If the wood of my loyalty is tested, he finds it solid; if my heart is fettered by his generosity, nothing releases it. May God Almighty perpetuate his authority and guard his blessing and his religion from others, by His grace. When the shaykh found in the assembly of the 'amid a respite and for logic a passage, he perused that so-and-so is frequenting the door, and is blessed by maintaining the rite of visitation. He does not complain of the burden of the embarrassment of the veil, but complains of his adornment by attending the door and the greeting.' He died on the morning of Sunday, before sunrise, the 16th of Rabi' al-Akhir, 465 AH, and was buried in the school next to the master Abu Ali al-Daqqaq.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage is a continuous biographical account of Imam Abu al-Qasim al-Qushayri (Zayn al-Islam), a leading Ash'ari theologian and Sufi master. It follows the author's sequence: first, it describes his comprehensive knowledge—including hadith, horsemanship, and the art of weapons—and his unique ability to address disciples' questions with subtle allusions and poetry. Next, it highlights his dictation sessions and his elegant writing style, then quotes a praise from Ali ibn al-Hasan's 'Damyat al-Qasr' extolling his rhetorical power and his mastery of the Ash'ari school. The biography then traces his Sufi lineage through a golden chain back to the Successors, emphasizing his spiritual authority. It proceeds to narrate the fitna (persecution) he faced around 440-455 AH due to sectarian partisanship, which forced him to flee to Baghdad, where he was honored by the caliph. After returning to Nishapur, he later enjoyed a decade of honor under Sultan Alp Arslan until his death in 465 AH. The passage concludes with a sample of his elegant prose and details of his death and burial beside Abu Ali al-Daqqaq. The commentary follows the author's narrative order, explaining each element—from his scholarly attainments, to his spiritual lineage, to his trials and final years—as a unified portrait of a multifaceted saint-scholar.
